<div class="side-box-flex">
<div class="side-box-image"><img alt="" data-file-height="878" data-file-width="604" decoding="async" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Yakh.svg/27px-Yakh.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Yakh.svg/41px-Yakh.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Yakh.svg/55px-Yakh.svg.png 2x" width="27"/></div>
<div class="side-box-text plainlist"><b>This article contains <a href="/wiki/Tifinagh" title="Tifinagh">Tifinagh text</a>.</b> Without proper <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Help:Multilingual_support_(Tifinagh)" title="Help:Multilingual support (Tifinagh)">rendering support</a>, you may see <a href="/wiki/Specials_(Unicode_block)#Replacement_character" title="Specials (Unicode block)">question marks, boxes, or other symbols</a> instead of <a href="/wiki/Tifinagh" title="Tifinagh">Tifinagh letters</a>.</div></div>
</div>
<p><b>Algeria</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[c]</a></sup> officially the <b>People's Democratic Republic of Algeria</b>, is a country in <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a>. Algeria is bordered to <a href="/wiki/Algeria%E2%80%93Tunisia_border" title="Algeria–Tunisia border">the northeast</a> by <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>; to <a href="/wiki/Algeria%E2%80%93Libya_border" title="Algeria–Libya border">the east</a> by <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>; to <a href="/wiki/Algeria%E2%80%93Niger_border" title="Algeria–Niger border">the southeast</a> by <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a>; to <a href="/wiki/Algeria%E2%80%93Western_Sahara_border" title="Algeria–Western Sahara border">the southwest</a> by <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a>; to <a href="/wiki/Algeria%E2%80%93Morocco_border" title="Algeria–Morocco border">the west</a> by <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>; and to the north by the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>. It is considered to be a part of the <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a> region of North Africa. It has a semi-arid geography, with most of the population living in the <a href="/wiki/Soil_fertility" title="Soil fertility">fertile</a> north and the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a> dominating the geography of the south. Algeria covers an area of 2,381,741 square kilometres (919,595 sq mi), making it the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">tenth largest nation by area</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_African_countries_by_area" title="List of African countries by area">largest nation in Africa</a>, being more than 200 times as large as the smallest country in the continent, <a href="/wiki/The_Gambia" title="The Gambia">The Gambia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[9]</a></sup> With a population of 44 million, Algeria is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_African_countries_by_population" title="List of African countries by population">ninth-most populous country</a> in Africa, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population" title="List of countries and dependencies by population">32nd-most populous country</a> in the world. The capital and <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Algeria" title="List of cities in Algeria">largest city</a> is <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a>, located in the far north on the Mediterranean coast.
</p><p>Algeria produced and is linked to many civilizations, empires and dynasties, including ancient <a href="/wiki/Numidia" title="Numidia">Numidians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenicians</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Punics" title="Punics">Carthaginians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vandal_Kingdom" title="Vandal Kingdom">Vandals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyads</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">Abbasids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rustamid_dynasty" title="Rustamid dynasty">Rustamids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Idrisid_dynasty" title="Idrisid dynasty">Idrisids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aghlabids" title="Aghlabids">Aghlabids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fatimid_Caliphate" title="Fatimid Caliphate">Fatimids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zirid_dynasty" title="Zirid dynasty">Zirids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hammadid_dynasty" title="Hammadid dynasty">Hammadids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Almoravid_dynasty" title="Almoravid dynasty">Almoravids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Almohad_Caliphate" title="Almohad Caliphate">Almohads</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zayyanid_dynasty" title="Zayyanid dynasty">Zayyanids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spaniards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottomans</a> and the <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French colonial empire</a>. The vast majority of Algeria's population is <a href="/wiki/Arab-Berber" title="Arab-Berber">Arab-Berber</a>, practicing <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Algeria" title="Islam in Algeria">Islam</a>, and using the official languages of <a href="/wiki/Modern_Standard_Arabic" title="Modern Standard Arabic">Arabic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">Berber</a>. However, <a href="/wiki/French_language_in_Algeria" title="French language in Algeria">French</a> serves as an administrative and educational language in some contexts. The main spoken language is <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Arabic" title="Algerian Arabic">Algerian Arabic</a>.
</p><p>Algeria is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential republic</a>, with local constituencies consisting of <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Algeria" title="Provinces of Algeria">58 provinces</a> and <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_Algeria" title="Communes of Algeria">1,541 communes</a>. Algeria is a <a href="/wiki/Regional_power" title="Regional power">regional power</a> in North Africa, and a <a href="/wiki/Middle_power" title="Middle power">middle power</a> in global affairs. It has the highest <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> of all non-island African countries and one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_African_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of African countries by GDP (nominal)">largest economies on the continent</a>, based largely on energy exports. Algeria has the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_proven_oil_reserves" title="List of countries by proven oil reserves">sixteenth-largest oil reserves</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_gas_proven_reserves" title="List of countries by natural gas proven reserves">ninth-largest reserves</a> of <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sonatrach" title="Sonatrach">Sonatrach</a>, the national oil company, is the largest company in Africa, supplying large amounts of <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> to Europe. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algerian_People%27s_National_Armed_Forces" title="Algerian People's National Armed Forces">Algeria's military</a> is one of the largest in Africa, and has the largest defence budget on the continent. It is a member of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">OIC</a>, <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Maghreb_Union" title="Arab Maghreb Union">Arab Maghreb Union</a>, of which it is a founding member.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Other forms of the name are: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ar">الجزائر</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic" title="Romanization of Arabic">romanized</a>: </small><span title="Arabic-language romanization"><i lang="ar-Latn">al-Jazāʾir</i></span>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algerian_Arabic_language" title="Algerian Arabic language">Algerian Arabic</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="arq">الدزاير</span>, <small>romanized: </small><span title="Algerian Arabic-language romanization"><i lang="arq-Latn">al-dzāyīr</i></span>; <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">Berber languages</a>: <span lang="ber">Lezzayer</span>; <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">Berber languages</a>: <span lang="ber">ⵍⴻⵣⴰⵢⴻⵔ</span>; <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">Berber languages</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ber">لزّاير</span>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Algérie</i>. It is officially the <b>People's Democratic Republic of Algeria</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[10]</a></sup> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ar">الجمهورية الجزائرية الديمقراطية الشعبية</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic" title="Romanization of Arabic">romanized</a>: </small><span title="Arabic-language romanization"><i lang="ar-Latn">al-Jumhūriyya al-Jazāʾiriyya ad-Dīmuqrāṭiyya aš-Šaʿbiyya</i></span>; <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">Berber languages</a>: <span lang="ber">Tagduda tamegdayt taɣerfant tazzayrit</span>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">Berber languages</a>: <span lang="ber">ⵜⴰⴳⴷⵓⴷⴰ ⵜⴰⵎⴳⴷⴰⵢⵜ ⵜⴰⵖⵔⴼⴰⵏⵜ ⵜⴰⴷⵣⴰⵢⵔⵉⵢⵜ</span>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[nb 1]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">Berber languages</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ber">تڨذوذا تازايريت تاماڨذايت تاغرفانت</span>;<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[nb 2]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">République algérienne démocratique et populaire</i>, abbreviated as RADP).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The country's name derives from the city of <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a> which in turn derives from the Arabic <span title="Arabic-language text"><i lang="ar-Latn">al-Jazāʾir</i></span> (<span title="Arabic-language text"><span dir="rtl" lang="ar">الجزائر</span></span>, "The Islands"),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[12]</a></sup> a truncated form of the older <span title="Arabic-language text"><i lang="ar-Latn">Jazāʾir Banī Mazghanna</i></span> (<span title="Arabic-language text"><span dir="rtl" lang="ar">جزائر بني مزغنة</span></span>, "Islands of the Mazghanna Tribe"),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-idrisi_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-idrisi-19">[14]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (February 2013)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-khaldun_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-khaldun-20">[15]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (February 2013)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup> employed by medieval geographers such as <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_al-Idrisi" title="Muhammad al-Idrisi">al-Idrisi</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Algeria" title="History of Algeria">History of Algeria</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory_and_ancient_history">Prehistory and ancient history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Prehistory and ancient history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_North_Africa" title="Prehistoric North Africa">Prehistoric North Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Africa_during_Antiquity" title="North Africa during Antiquity">North Africa during Antiquity</a></div>
<p>Around ~1.8-million-year-old stone artifacts from Ain Hanech (Algeria) were considered to represent the oldest archaeological materials in North Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-science.org_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-science.org-21">[16]</a></sup> Stone artifacts and cut-marked bones that were excavated from two nearby deposits at Ain Boucherit are estimated to be ~1.9 million years old, and even older stone artifacts to be as old as ~2.4 million years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-science.org_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-science.org-21">[16]</a></sup> Hence, the Ain Boucherit evidence shows that ancestral hominins inhabited the Mediterranean fringe in northern Africa much earlier than previously thought. The evidence strongly argues for early dispersal of stone tool manufacture and use from East Africa, or a possible multiple-origin scenario of stone technology in both East and North Africa.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dj%C3%A9mila-109038.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="501" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Dj%C3%A9mila-109038.jpg/220px-Dj%C3%A9mila-109038.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Dj%C3%A9mila-109038.jpg/330px-Dj%C3%A9mila-109038.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Dj%C3%A9mila-109038.jpg/440px-Dj%C3%A9mila-109038.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dj%C3%A9mila-109038.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Roman ruins at <a href="/wiki/Dj%C3%A9mila" title="Djémila">Djémila</a></div></div></div>
<p>Neanderthal tool makers produced hand axes in the <a href="/wiki/Levallois_technique" title="Levallois technique">Levalloisian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mousterian" title="Mousterian">Mousterian</a> styles (43,000 BC) similar to those in the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[18]</a></sup> Algeria was the site of the highest state of development of <a href="/wiki/Middle_Paleolithic" title="Middle Paleolithic">Middle Paleolithic</a> <a href="/wiki/Flake_tool" title="Flake tool">Flake tool</a> techniques.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DelsonTattersall2004_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-DelsonTattersall2004-24">[19]</a></sup> Tools of this era, starting about 30,000 BC, are called <a href="/wiki/Aterian" title="Aterian">Aterian</a> (after the archaeological site of <a href="/wiki/Bir_el_Ater" title="Bir el Ater">Bir el Ater</a>, south of <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A9bessa" title="Tébessa">Tebessa</a>).
</p><p>The earliest blade industries in North Africa are called <a href="/wiki/Iberomaurusian" title="Iberomaurusian">Iberomaurusian</a> (located mainly in the <a href="/wiki/Oran" title="Oran">Oran</a> region). This industry appears to have spread throughout the coastal regions of the <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a> between 15,000 and 10,000 BC. <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic civilization</a> (animal domestication and agriculture) developed in the Saharan and Mediterranean Maghreb perhaps as early as 11,000 BC<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[20]</a></sup> or as late as between 6000 and 2000 BC. This life, richly depicted in the <a href="/wiki/Tassili_n%27Ajjer" title="Tassili n'Ajjer">Tassili n'Ajjer</a> paintings, predominated in Algeria until the classical period. The mixture of peoples of North Africa coalesced eventually into a distinct native population that came to be called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berber_people" title="Berber people">Berbers</a>, who are the indigenous peoples of northern Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[21]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Timgad_rue.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Timgad_rue.jpg/220px-Timgad_rue.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Timgad_rue.jpg/330px-Timgad_rue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Timgad_rue.jpg/440px-Timgad_rue.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Timgad_rue.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ancient <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a> ruins of <a href="/wiki/Timgad" title="Timgad">Timgad</a> on the street leading to the local <a href="/wiki/Arch_of_Trajan_(Timgad)" title="Arch of Trajan (Timgad)">Arch of Trajan</a></div></div></div>
<p>From their principal center of power at <a href="/wiki/Carthage" title="Carthage">Carthage</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carthaginians" title="Carthaginians">Carthaginians</a> expanded and established small settlements along the North African coast; by 600 BC, a <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenician</a> presence existed at <a href="/wiki/Tipasa" title="Tipasa">Tipasa</a>, east of <a href="/wiki/Cherchell" title="Cherchell">Cherchell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hippo_Regius" title="Hippo Regius">Hippo Regius</a> (modern <a href="/wiki/Annaba" title="Annaba">Annaba</a>) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rusicade" title="Rusicade">Rusicade</a> (modern <a href="/wiki/Skikda" title="Skikda">Skikda</a>). These settlements served as market towns as well as anchorages.
</p><p>As Carthaginian power grew, its impact on the indigenous population increased dramatically. Berber civilisation was already at a stage in which agriculture, manufacturing, trade, and political organisation supported several states. Trade links between Carthage and the Berbers in the interior grew, but territorial expansion also resulted in the enslavement or military recruitment of some Berbers and in the extraction of tribute from others.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GM_Massinissa.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="862" data-file-width="865" decoding="async" height="219" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/GM_Massinissa.png/220px-GM_Massinissa.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/GM_Massinissa.png/330px-GM_Massinissa.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/GM_Massinissa.png/440px-GM_Massinissa.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GM_Massinissa.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Masinissa" title="Masinissa">Masinissa</a> (c. 238–148 BC), first king of Numidia</div></div></div>
<p>By the early 4th century BC, Berbers formed the single largest element of the Carthaginian army. In the <a href="/wiki/Mercenary_War" title="Mercenary War">Revolt of the Mercenaries</a>, Berber soldiers rebelled from 241 to 238 BC after being unpaid following the defeat of Carthage in the <a href="/wiki/First_Punic_War" title="First Punic War">First Punic War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fischer-Bovet2014_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fischer-Bovet2014-27">[22]</a></sup> They succeeded in obtaining control of much of Carthage's North African territory, and they minted coins bearing the name Libyan, used in Greek to describe natives of North Africa. The Carthaginian state declined because of successive defeats by the Romans in the <a href="/wiki/Punic_Wars" title="Punic Wars">Punic Wars</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spielvogel2014_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Spielvogel2014-28">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 146 BC the city of <a href="/wiki/Carthage" title="Carthage">Carthage</a> was destroyed. As Carthaginian power waned, the influence of Berber leaders in the hinterland grew. By the 2nd century BC, several large but loosely administered Berber kingdoms had emerged. Two of them were established in <a href="/wiki/Numidia" title="Numidia">Numidia</a>, behind the coastal areas controlled by Carthage. West of Numidia lay <a href="/wiki/Mauretania" title="Mauretania">Mauretania</a>, which extended across the <a href="/wiki/Moulouya_River" title="Moulouya River">Moulouya River</a> in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> to the Atlantic Ocean. The high point of Berber civilisation, unequalled until the coming of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Almohads" title="Almohads">Almohads</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Almoravids" title="Almoravids">Almoravids</a> more than a millennium later, was reached during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Masinissa" title="Masinissa">Masinissa</a> in the 2nd century BC.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Justinian555AD.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1144" data-file-width="2111" decoding="async" height="119" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Justinian555AD.png/220px-Justinian555AD.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Justinian555AD.png/330px-Justinian555AD.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Justinian555AD.png/440px-Justinian555AD.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Justinian555AD.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The lands which comprise modern day Algeria were part of the Byzantine Empire (The empire in 555 under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Justinian_the_Great" title="Justinian the Great">Justinian the Great</a>, at its greatest extent since the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a> (<a href="/wiki/Vassal_state" title="Vassal state">vassals</a> in pink))</div></div></div>
<p>After Masinissa's death in 148 BC, the Berber kingdoms were divided and reunited several times. Masinissa's line survived until 24 AD, when the remaining Berber territory was annexed to the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Side_face_(2).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4408" data-file-width="3145" decoding="async" height="308" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Side_face_%282%29.jpg/220px-Side_face_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Side_face_%282%29.jpg/330px-Side_face_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Side_face_%282%29.jpg/440px-Side_face_%282%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Side_face_(2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Roman inscription from Agueneb in the province of Laghouat</div></div></div>
<p>For several centuries Algeria was ruled by the Romans, who founded many colonies in the region. Like the rest of North Africa, Algeria was one of the breadbaskets of the empire, exporting cereals and other agricultural products. <a href="/wiki/Augustine_of_Hippo" title="Augustine of Hippo">Saint Augustine</a> was the bishop of <a href="/wiki/Hippo_Regius" title="Hippo Regius">Hippo Regius</a> (modern-day Annaba, Algeria), located in the Roman province of <a href="/wiki/Africa_(Roman_province)" title="Africa (Roman province)">Africa</a>. The Germanic <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">Vandals</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geiseric" title="Geiseric">Geiseric</a> moved into North Africa in 429, and by 435 controlled coastal Numidia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vandaf_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-vandaf-29">[24]</a></sup> They did not make any significant settlement on the land, as they were harassed by local tribes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In fact, by the time the Byzantines arrived <a href="/wiki/Leptis_Magna" title="Leptis Magna">Leptis Magna</a> was abandoned and the Msellata region was occupied by the indigenous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazigh" title="Amazigh">Laguatan</a> who had been busy facilitating an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazigh" title="Amazigh">Amazigh</a> political, military and cultural revival.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vandaf_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-vandaf-29">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[25]</a></sup> Furthermore, during the rule of the Romans, Byzantines, Vandals, Carthaginians, and Ottomans the Berber people were the only or one of the few in North Africa who remained independent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto3_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto3-32">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[29]</a></sup> The Berber people were so resistant that even during the Muslim conquest of North Africa they still had control and possession over their mountains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[31]</a></sup>
</p><p>The collapse of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a> led to the establishment of a native Kingdom based in Altava (modern day Algeria) known as the <a href="/wiki/Mauro-Roman_Kingdom" title="Mauro-Roman Kingdom">Mauro-Roman Kingdom</a>. It was succeeded by another Kingdom based in Altava, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Altava" title="Kingdom of Altava">Kingdom of Altava</a>. During the reign of Kusaila its territory extended from the region of modern-day <a href="/wiki/Fez,_Morocco" title="Fez, Morocco">Fez</a> in the west to the western <a href="/wiki/Aur%C3%A8s" title="Aurès">Aurès</a> and later <a href="/wiki/Kairouan" title="Kairouan">Kairaouan</a> and the interior of Ifriqiya in the east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[37]</a></sup>
</p><p>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Medieval_Muslim_Algeria" title="Medieval Muslim Algeria">Medieval Muslim Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mansourah-1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Mansourah-1.jpg/220px-Mansourah-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Mansourah-1.jpg/330px-Mansourah-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Mansourah-1.jpg/440px-Mansourah-1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mansourah-1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mansourah mosque, Tlemcen</div></div></div>
<p>After negligible resistance from the locals, <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslim</a> <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyad Caliphate</a> conquered Algeria in the early 8th century.
</p><p>Large numbers of the indigenous Berber people converted to Islam. Christians, Berber and Latin speakers remained in the great majority in Tunisia until the end of the 9th century and Muslims only became a vast majority some time in the 10th.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jonathan_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-jonathan-43">[38]</a></sup> After the fall of the Umayyad Caliphate, numerous local dynasties emerged, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rustamids" title="Rustamids">Rustamids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aghlabids" title="Aghlabids">Aghlabids</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fatimids" title="Fatimids">Fatimids</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zirids" title="Zirids">Zirids</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hammadids" title="Hammadids">Hammadids</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Almoravids" title="Almoravids">Almoravids</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Almohads" title="Almohads">Almohads</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abdalwadid" title="Abdalwadid">Abdalwadid</a>. The Christians left in three waves: after the initial conquest, in the 10th century and the 11th. The last were evacuated to Sicily by the Normans and the few remaining died out in the 14th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jonathan_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-jonathan-43">[38]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fatimid.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1931" data-file-width="3466" decoding="async" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Fatimid.jpg/220px-Fatimid.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Fatimid.jpg/330px-Fatimid.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Fatimid.jpg/440px-Fatimid.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fatimid.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fatimid Caliphate, a <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia</a> <a href="/wiki/Isma%27ilism" title="Isma'ilism">Ismaili</a> dynasty that ruled much of North Africa, c. 960–1100</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Statue_of_Dyhia_in_Khenchela_(Algeria).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1344" data-file-width="738" decoding="async" height="310" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Statue_of_Dyhia_in_Khenchela_%28Algeria%29.jpg/170px-Statue_of_Dyhia_in_Khenchela_%28Algeria%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Statue_of_Dyhia_in_Khenchela_%28Algeria%29.jpg/255px-Statue_of_Dyhia_in_Khenchela_%28Algeria%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Statue_of_Dyhia_in_Khenchela_%28Algeria%29.jpg/340px-Statue_of_Dyhia_in_Khenchela_%28Algeria%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Statue_of_Dyhia_in_Khenchela_(Algeria).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dihya" title="Dihya">Dihya</a> memorial in <a href="/wiki/Khenchela" title="Khenchela">Khenchela</a>, Algeria</div></div></div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, North Africa was home to many great scholars, saints and sovereigns including <a href="/wiki/Judah_ibn_Kuraish" title="Judah ibn Kuraish">Judah Ibn Quraysh</a>, the first grammarian to mention Semitic and Berber languages, the great Sufi masters <a href="/wiki/Abu_Madyan" title="Abu Madyan">Sidi Boumediene (Abu Madyan)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sidi_El_Houari" title="Sidi El Houari">Sidi El Houari</a>, and the Emirs <a href="/wiki/Abd_al-Mu%27min" title="Abd al-Mu'min">Abd Al Mu'min</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yaghmurasen_Ibn_Zyan" title="Yaghmurasen Ibn Zyan">Yāghmūrasen</a>. It was during this time that the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fatimids" title="Fatimids">Fatimids</a> or children of Fatima, daughter of Muhammad, came to the Maghreb. These "Fatimids" went on to found a long lasting dynasty stretching across the Maghreb, Hejaz and the Levant, boasting a secular inner government, as well as a powerful army and navy, made up primarily of <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levantines</a> extending from Algeria to their capital state of <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fatimid_caliphate" title="Fatimid caliphate">Fatimid caliphate</a> began to collapse when its governors the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zirids" title="Zirids">Zirids</a> seceded. In order to punish them the Fatimids sent the Arab <a href="/wiki/Banu_Hilal" title="Banu Hilal">Banu Hilal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Banu_Sulaym" title="Banu Sulaym">Banu Sulaym</a> against them. The resultant war is recounted in the epic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taghribat_Bani_Hilal" title="Taghribat Bani Hilal">Tāghribāt</a>. In Al-Tāghrībāt the Amazigh Zirid Hero <a href="/wiki/Khalifa_al-Zanati" title="Khalifa al-Zanati">Khālīfā Al-Zānatī</a> asks daily, for duels, to defeat the Hilalan hero <a href="/wiki/Abu_Zayd_al-Hilali" title="Abu Zayd al-Hilali">Ābu Zayd al-Hilalī</a> and many other Arab knights in a string of victories. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zirid" title="Zirid">Zirids</a>, however, were ultimately defeated ushering in an adoption of Arab customs and culture. The indigenous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berber_people" title="Berber people">Amazigh</a> tribes, however, remained largely independent, and depending on tribe, location and time controlled varying parts of the Maghreb, at times unifying it (as under the Fatimids). The Fatimid Islamic state, also known as <a href="/wiki/Fatimid_Caliphate" title="Fatimid Caliphate">Fatimid Caliphate</a> made an Islamic empire that included North Africa, Sicily, <a href="/wiki/Palestine_(region)" title="Palestine (region)">Palestine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> coast of Africa, Tihamah, <a href="/wiki/Hejaz" title="Hejaz">Hejaz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[41]</a></sup> Caliphates from Northern Africa traded with the other empires of their time, as well as forming part of a confederated support and trade network with other Islamic states during the Islamic Era.
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berber_people" title="Berber people">Berber people</a> historically consisted of several tribes. The two main branches were the Botr and Barnès tribes, who were divided into tribes, and again into sub-tribes. Each region of the Maghreb contained several tribes (for example, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sanhadja" title="Sanhadja">Sanhadja</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Houara" title="Houara">Houara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zenata" title="Zenata">Zenata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Masmuda" title="Masmuda">Masmouda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kutama" title="Kutama">Kutama</a>, Awarba, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berghwata" title="Berghwata">Berghwata</a>). All these tribes made independent territorial decisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[42]</a></sup>
</p><p>Several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berber_people" title="Berber people">Amazigh</a> dynasties emerged during the Middle Ages in the Maghreb and other nearby lands. <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Khaldun" title="Ibn Khaldun">Ibn Khaldun</a> provides a table summarising the Amazigh dynasties of the Maghreb region, the <a href="/wiki/Zirid_dynasty" title="Zirid dynasty">Zirid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Tlemcen" title="Emirate of Tlemcen">Ifranid</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maghrawid_Dynasty" title="Maghrawid Dynasty">Maghrawa</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Almoravid" title="Almoravid">Almoravid</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hammadid" title="Hammadid">Hammadid</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Almohad" title="Almohad">Almohad</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merinid" title="Merinid">Merinid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zayyanid_dynasty" title="Zayyanid dynasty">Abdalwadid</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wattasid" title="Wattasid">Wattasid</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meknassa" title="Meknassa">Meknassa</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hafsid" title="Hafsid">Hafsid</a> dynasties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[43]</a></sup> Both of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hammadid" title="Hammadid">Hammadid</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zirid" title="Zirid">Zirid</a> empires as well as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fatimid" title="Fatimid">Fatimids</a> established their rule in all of the Maghreb countries. The <a href="/wiki/Zirid_dynasty" title="Zirid dynasty">Zirids</a> ruled land in what is now Algeria, Tunisia, Morocco, Libya, Spain, Malta and Italy. The <a href="/wiki/Hammadid_dynasty" title="Hammadid dynasty">Hammadids</a> captured and held important regions such as Ouargla, Constantine, Sfax, Susa, Algiers, Tripoli and Fez establishing their rule in every country in the Maghreb region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[46]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Fatimid_Caliphate" title="Fatimid Caliphate">Fatimids</a> which was created and established by the Kutama Berbers <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto2_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-52">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-53">[48]</a></sup> conquered all of North Africa as well as Sicily and parts of the Middle East.
</p><p><b>A few examples of medieval Berber dynasties which originated in Modern Algeria </b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Tlemcen" title="Emirate of Tlemcen">Ifranid Dynasty</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maghrawid_Dynasty" title="Maghrawid Dynasty">Maghrawa Dynasty</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zirid_dynasty" title="Zirid dynasty">Zirid dynasty</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hammadid_dynasty" title="Hammadid dynasty">Hammadid dynasty</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fatimid_Caliphate" title="Fatimid Caliphate">Fatimid Caliphate</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto2_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-52">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-53">[48]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Tlemcen" title="Kingdom of Tlemcen">Kingdom of Tlemcen</a></li></ul>
<p>Following the Berber revolt numerous independent states emerged across the Maghreb. In Algeria the <a href="/wiki/Rustamid_dynasty" title="Rustamid dynasty">Rustamid Kingdom</a> was established. The Rustamid realm stretched from Tafilalt in Morocco to the Nafusa mountains in Libya including south, central and western Tunisia therefore including territory in all of the modern day Maghreb countries, in the south the Rustamid realm expanded to the modern borders of <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a> and included territory in <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[51]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Zirid_Dynasty.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="751" data-file-width="1125" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/The_Zirid_Dynasty.jpg/220px-The_Zirid_Dynasty.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/The_Zirid_Dynasty.jpg/330px-The_Zirid_Dynasty.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/The_Zirid_Dynasty.jpg/440px-The_Zirid_Dynasty.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Zirid_Dynasty.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing territories that were controlled by the Zirid Dynasty</div></div></div>
<p>Once extending their control over all of the Maghreb, part of Spain<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[52]</a></sup> and briefly over Sicily,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[53]</a></sup> originating from modern Algeria, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zirids" title="Zirids">Zirids</a> only controlled modern <a href="/wiki/Ifriqiya" title="Ifriqiya">Ifriqiya</a> by the 11th century. The Zirids recognized nominal suzerainty of the Fatimid caliphs of Cairo. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=El_Mu%27izz&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="El Mu'izz (page does not exist)">El Mu'izz</a> the Zirid ruler decided to end this recognition and declared his independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-60">[55]</a></sup> The Zirids also fought against other Zenata Kingdoms, for example the Maghrawa, a Berber dynasty originating from Algeria and which at one point was a dominant power in the Maghreb ruling over much of Morocco and western Algeria including Fez, Sijilmasa, Aghmat, Oujda, most of the Sous and Draa and reaching as far as M'sila and the Zab in Algeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[59]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maghrawa_dynasty_-_dynastie_maghraoua.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1203" data-file-width="1125" decoding="async" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Maghrawa_dynasty_-_dynastie_maghraoua.jpg/220px-Maghrawa_dynasty_-_dynastie_maghraoua.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Maghrawa_dynasty_-_dynastie_maghraoua.jpg/330px-Maghrawa_dynasty_-_dynastie_maghraoua.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Maghrawa_dynasty_-_dynastie_maghraoua.jpg/440px-Maghrawa_dynasty_-_dynastie_maghraoua.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maghrawa_dynasty_-_dynastie_maghraoua.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Territories controlled by the Maghrawa</div></div></div>
<p>As the Fatimid state was at the time too weak to attempt a direct invasion, they found another means of revenge. Between the <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">Nile</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> were living <a href="/wiki/Bedouin" title="Bedouin">Bedouin</a> nomad tribes expelled from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabia" title="Arabia">Arabia</a> for their disruption and turbulency. The <a href="/wiki/Banu_Hilal" title="Banu Hilal">Banu Hilal</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Banu_Sulaym" title="Banu Sulaym">Banu Sulaym</a> for example, who regularly disrupted farmers in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nile_Valley" title="Nile Valley">Nile Valley</a> since the nomads would often loot their farms. The then <a href="/wiki/Fatimid_Caliphate" title="Fatimid Caliphate">Fatimid</a> vizier decided to destroy what he couldn't control, and broke a deal with the chiefs of these Beduouin tribes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[60]</a></sup> The Fatimids even gave them money to leave.
</p><p>Whole tribes set off with women, children, elders, animals and camping equipment. Some stopped on the way, especially in <a href="/wiki/Cyrenaica" title="Cyrenaica">Cyrenaica</a>, where they are still one of the essential elements of the settlement but most arrived in <a href="/wiki/Ifriqiya" title="Ifriqiya">Ifriqiya</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Gab%C3%A8s_Governorate" title="Gabès Governorate">Gabes</a> region, arriving 1051.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[61]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zirid" title="Zirid">Zirid</a> ruler tried to stop this rising tide, but with each encounter, the last under the walls of <a href="/wiki/Kairouan" title="Kairouan">Kairouan</a>, his troops were defeated and the Arabs remained masters of the battlefield. The Arabs usually didn't take control over the cities, instead looting them and destroying them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-60">[55]</a></sup>
</p><p>The invasion kept going, and in 1057 the Arabs spread on the high plains of <a href="/wiki/Constantine,_Algeria" title="Constantine, Algeria">Constantine</a> where they encircled the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beni_Hammad_Fort" title="Beni Hammad Fort">Qalaa of Banu Hammad</a> (capital of the <a href="/wiki/Hammadid_dynasty" title="Hammadid dynasty">Hammadid Emirate</a>), as they had done in Kairouan a few decades ago. From there they gradually gained the upper <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oran" title="Oran">Oran</a> plains. Some of these territories were forcibly taken back by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Almohads" title="Almohads">Almohads</a> in the second half of the 12th century. The influx of <a href="/wiki/Bedouin" title="Bedouin">Bedouin</a> tribes was a major factor in the linguistic, cultural <a href="/wiki/Arabization" title="Arabization">Arabization</a> of the Maghreb and in the spread of <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomadism</a> in areas where <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a> had previously been dominant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[62]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Khaldun" title="Ibn Khaldun">Ibn Khaldun</a> noted that the lands ravaged by <a href="/wiki/Banu_Hilal" title="Banu Hilal">Banu Hilal</a> tribes had become completely arid desert.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[63]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Almohad_Caliphate" title="Almohad Caliphate">Almohads</a> originating from modern day Morocco, although founded by a man originating from Algeria<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[64]</a></sup> known as <a href="/wiki/Abd_al-Mu%27min" title="Abd al-Mu'min">Abd al-Mu'min</a> would soon take control over the Maghreb. During the time of the Almohad Dynasty <a href="/wiki/Abd_al-Mu%27min" title="Abd al-Mu'min">Abd al-Mu'min</a>'s tribe, the Koumïa, were the main supporters of the throne and the most important body of the empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[65]</a></sup> Defeating the weakening <a href="/wiki/Almoravid_dynasty" title="Almoravid dynasty">Almoravid Empire</a> and taking control over Morocco in 1147,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[66]</a></sup> they pushed into Algeria in 1152, taking control over Tlemcen, Oran, and Algiers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-72">[67]</a></sup> wrestling control from the Hilian Arabs, and by the same year they defeated Hammadids who controlled Eastern Algeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-72">[67]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ifranid_Dynasty.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="947" data-file-width="1124" decoding="async" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Ifranid_Dynasty.jpg/220px-Ifranid_Dynasty.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Ifranid_Dynasty.jpg/330px-Ifranid_Dynasty.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Ifranid_Dynasty.jpg/440px-Ifranid_Dynasty.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ifranid_Dynasty.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lands ruled by the Ifrenid dynasty of Tlemcen (Current day Algeria) Partially based on the book of Ibn Khaldun: <i>The History of the Berbers</i></div></div></div><p>
Following their decisive defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Las_Navas_de_Tolosa" title="Battle of Las Navas de Tolosa">Battle of Las Navas de Tolosa</a> in 1212 the Almohads began collapsing, and in 1235 the governor of modern-day Western Algeria, <a href="/wiki/Yaghmurasen_Ibn_Zyan" title="Yaghmurasen Ibn Zyan">Yaghmurasen Ibn Zyan</a> declared his independence and established the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Tlemcen" title="Kingdom of Tlemcen">Kingdom of Tlemcen</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Zayyanid_dynasty" title="Zayyanid dynasty">Zayyanid dynasty</a>. Warring with the Almohad forces attempting to restore control over Algeria for 13 years, they defeated the Almohads in 1248 after killing their Caliph in a successful ambush near Oujda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[68]</a></sup> </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Zayyanid_Kingdom_-_Royaume_Zianide.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="595" data-file-width="1125" decoding="async" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Zayyanid_Kingdom_-_Royaume_Zianide.jpg/220px-Zayyanid_Kingdom_-_Royaume_Zianide.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Zayyanid_Kingdom_-_Royaume_Zianide.jpg/330px-Zayyanid_Kingdom_-_Royaume_Zianide.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Zayyanid_Kingdom_-_Royaume_Zianide.jpg/440px-Zayyanid_Kingdom_-_Royaume_Zianide.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Zayyanid_Kingdom_-_Royaume_Zianide.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Zayyanid Kingdom of Tlemcen during the rule of Abu Malek</div></div></div>
<p>The Zayyanids retained their control over Algeria for 3 centuries. Much of the eastern territories of Algeria were under the authority of the <a href="/wiki/Hafsid_dynasty" title="Hafsid dynasty">Hafsid dynasty</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[69]</a></sup> although the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hafsids_of_Beja%C3%AFa" title="Hafsids of Bejaïa">Emirate of Bejaia</a> encompassing the Algerian territories of the Hafsids would occasionally be independent from central Tunisian control. At their peak the Zayyanid kingdom included all of Morocco as its vassal to the west and in the east reached as far as <a href="/wiki/Tunis" title="Tunis">Tunis</a> which they captured during the reign of Abu Tashfin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constantine2_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Constantine2-77">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constantine_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Constantine-78">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cour_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cour-79">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arnolet_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Arnolet-80">[75]</a></sup>
</p><p>After several conflicts with local <a href="/wiki/Barbary_pirates" title="Barbary pirates">Barbary pirates</a> sponsored by the Zayyanid sultans,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[76]</a></sup> Spain decided to invade Algeria and defeat the native Kingdom of Tlemcen. In 1505, they <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Mers-el-K%C3%A9bir_(1505)" title="Capture of Mers-el-Kébir (1505)">invaded and captured Mers el Kébir</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[77]</a></sup> and in 1509 after a bloody siege, they <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_Oran_(1509)" title="Spanish conquest of Oran (1509)">conquered Oran</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[78]</a></sup> Following their decisive victories over the Algerians in the western-coastal areas of Algeria, the Spanish decided to get bolder, and invaded more Algerian cities. In 1510, they led a series of sieges and attacks, taking over Bejaia <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capture_of_Bejaia_(1510)" title="Capture of Bejaia (1510)">in a large siege</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[79]</a></sup> and leading a <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Siege_of_Algiers_(1510)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Siege of Algiers (1510) (page does not exist)">semi-successful siege against Algiers</a>. They also besieged Tlemcen. In 1511, they took control over <a href="/wiki/Cherchell" title="Cherchell">Cherchell</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[80]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Jijel" title="Jijel">Jijel</a>, and attacked <a href="/wiki/Mostaganem" title="Mostaganem">Mostaganem</a> where although they weren't able to conquer the city, they were able to force a tribute on them.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ottoman_era">Ottoman era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Ottoman era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Algeria" title="Ottoman Algeria">Ottoman Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maghreb_15th_Century.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1185" data-file-width="3127" decoding="async" height="95" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Maghreb_15th_Century.svg/250px-Maghreb_15th_Century.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Maghreb_15th_Century.svg/375px-Maghreb_15th_Century.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Maghreb_15th_Century.svg/500px-Maghreb_15th_Century.svg.png 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maghreb_15th_Century.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Tlemcen" title="Kingdom of Tlemcen">Zayyanid kingdom</a> of Tlemcen in the fifteenth century and its neighbors</div></div></div>
<p>In 1516, the Ottoman privateer brothers <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aruj" title="Aruj">Aruj</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hayreddin_Barbarossa" title="Hayreddin Barbarossa">Hayreddin Barbarossa</a>, who operated successfully under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hafsids" title="Hafsids">Hafsids</a>, moved their base of operations to Algiers. They succeeded in conquering Jijel and Algiers from the <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spaniards</a> with help from the locals who saw them as liberators from the Christians, but the brothers eventually assassinated the local noble <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Salim_al-Tumi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Salim al-Tumi (page does not exist)">Salim al-Tumi</a> and took control over the city and the surrounding regions. When Aruj was killed in 1518 during his <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Tlemcen_(1518)" title="Fall of Tlemcen (1518)">invasion of Tlemcen</a>, Hayreddin succeeded him as military commander of Algiers. The <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> sultan gave him the title of <a href="/wiki/Beylerbey" title="Beylerbey">beylerbey</a> and a contingent of some 2,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Janissaries" title="Janissaries">janissaries</a>. With the aid of this force and native Algerians, <a href="/wiki/Hayreddin_Barbarossa" title="Hayreddin Barbarossa">Hayreddin</a> conquered the whole area between Constantine and Oran (although the city of Oran remained in Spanish hands until 1792).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-csa16_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-csa16-86">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mikaberidze_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mikaberidze-87">[82]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Barbarossa_Hayreddin_Pasha.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="787" data-file-width="572" decoding="async" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Barbarossa_Hayreddin_Pasha.jpg/170px-Barbarossa_Hayreddin_Pasha.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Barbarossa_Hayreddin_Pasha.jpg/255px-Barbarossa_Hayreddin_Pasha.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Barbarossa_Hayreddin_Pasha.jpg/340px-Barbarossa_Hayreddin_Pasha.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Barbarossa_Hayreddin_Pasha.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hayreddin_Barbarossa" title="Hayreddin Barbarossa">Hayreddin Barbarossa</a></div></div></div>
<p>The next beylerbey was Hayreddin's son <a href="/wiki/Hasan_Pasha_(son_of_Barbarossa)" title="Hasan Pasha (son of Barbarossa)">Hasan</a>, who assumed the position in 1544. He was a <a href="/wiki/Kouloughlis" title="Kouloughlis">Kouloughli</a> or of mixed origins, as his mother was an Algerian Mooresse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[83]</a></sup> Until 1587 Beylerbeylik of Algiers was governed by Beylerbeys who served terms with no fixed limits. Subsequently, with the institution of a regular administration, governors with the title of pasha ruled for three-year terms. The pasha was assisted by an autonomous janissary unit, known in Algeria as the <a href="/wiki/Odjak_of_Algiers" title="Odjak of Algiers">Ojaq</a> who were led by an <a href="/wiki/Agha_of_the_Janissaries" title="Agha of the Janissaries">agha</a>. Discontent among the ojaq rose in the mid-1600s because they were not paid regularly, and they repeatedly revolted against the pasha. As a result, the agha charged the pasha with corruption and incompetence and seized power in 1659.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-csa16_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-csa16-86">[81]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Plague_(disease)" title="Plague (disease)">Plague</a> had repeatedly struck the cities of North Africa. Algiers lost between 30,000 and 50,000 inhabitants to the plague in 1620–21, and had high fatalities in 1654–57, 1665, 1691 and 1740–42.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davis_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Davis-89">[84]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Debarquement_et_maltraitement_de_prisonniers_a_alger.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="839" data-file-width="1121" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Debarquement_et_maltraitement_de_prisonniers_a_alger.JPG/220px-Debarquement_et_maltraitement_de_prisonniers_a_alger.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Debarquement_et_maltraitement_de_prisonniers_a_alger.JPG/330px-Debarquement_et_maltraitement_de_prisonniers_a_alger.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Debarquement_et_maltraitement_de_prisonniers_a_alger.JPG/440px-Debarquement_et_maltraitement_de_prisonniers_a_alger.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Debarquement_et_maltraitement_de_prisonniers_a_alger.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Slavery in the Ottoman Empire">Christian slaves</a> in Algiers, 1706</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Barbary_pirates" title="Barbary pirates">Barbary pirates</a> preyed on Christian and other non-Islamic shipping in the western Mediterranean Sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davis_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-Davis-89">[84]</a></sup> The pirates often took the passengers and crew on the ships and sold them or used them as <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slaves</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hannay_1911_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hannay_1911-90">[85]</a></sup> They also did a brisk business in ransoming some of the captives. According to Robert Davis, from the 16th to 19th century, pirates captured 1 million to 1.25 million Europeans as slaves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barbary_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-barbary-91">[86]</a></sup> They often made raids on European coastal towns to capture Christian slaves to sell at <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Slavery in the Ottoman Empire">slave markets</a> in North Africa and other parts of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[87]</a></sup> In 1544, for example, <a href="/wiki/Hayreddin_Barbarossa" title="Hayreddin Barbarossa">Hayreddin Barbarossa</a> captured the island of <a href="/wiki/Ischia" title="Ischia">Ischia</a>, taking 4,000 prisoners, and enslaved some 9,000 inhabitants of <a href="/wiki/Lipari" title="Lipari">Lipari</a>, almost the entire population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[88]</a></sup> In 1551, the Ottoman governor of Algiers, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turgut_Reis" title="Turgut Reis">Turgut Reis</a>, enslaved the entire population of the <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Maltese</a> island of <a href="/wiki/Gozo" title="Gozo">Gozo</a>. Barbary pirates often attacked the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a>. The threat was so severe that residents abandoned the island of <a href="/wiki/Formentera" title="Formentera">Formentera</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[89]</a></sup> The introduction of broad-sail ships from the beginning of the 17th century allowed them to branch out into the Atlantic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Auchterlonie2012_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Auchterlonie2012-95">[90]</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 1627 two pirate ships from Algiers under the command of <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> pirate <a href="/wiki/Jan_Janszoon" title="Jan Janszoon">Jan Janszoon</a> sailed as far as <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[91]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Abductions" title="Turkish Abductions">raiding and capturing slaves</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[94]</a></sup> Two weeks earlier another pirate ship from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sale,_Morocco" title="Sale, Morocco">Salé</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saadi_dynasty" title="Saadi dynasty">Morocco</a> had also raided in Iceland. Some of the slaves brought to Algiers were later ransomed back to Iceland, but some chose to stay in Algeria. In 1629, pirate ships from Algeria raided the <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">Faroe Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[95]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1671, the taifa of raises, or the company of corsair captains rebelled, killed the agha, and placed one of its own in power. The new leader received the title of <a href="/wiki/Dey" title="Dey">Dey</a>. After 1689, the right to select the dey passed to the <a href="/wiki/Divan" title="Divan">divan</a>, a council of some sixty nobles. It was at first dominated by the <i><a href="/wiki/Ojaq" title="Ojaq">ojaq</a></i>; but by the 18th century, it had become the dey's instrument. In 1710, the dey persuaded the sultan to recognise him and his successors as regent, replacing the <a href="/wiki/Pasha" title="Pasha">pasha</a> in that role. Although Algiers remained nominally part of the Ottoman Empire,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-csa16_86-2"><a href="#cite_note-csa16-86">[81]</a></sup> in reality they acted independently from the rest of the Empire,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[97]</a></sup> and often had wars with other Ottoman subjects and territories such as the <a href="/wiki/Beylik_of_Tunis" title="Beylik of Tunis">Beylik of Tunis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[98]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kabyle_Kingdoms_in_the_Ottoman_era_at_their_height_.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1587" data-file-width="1125" decoding="async" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Kabyle_Kingdoms_in_the_Ottoman_era_at_their_height_.jpg/170px-Kabyle_Kingdoms_in_the_Ottoman_era_at_their_height_.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Kabyle_Kingdoms_in_the_Ottoman_era_at_their_height_.jpg/255px-Kabyle_Kingdoms_in_the_Ottoman_era_at_their_height_.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Kabyle_Kingdoms_in_the_Ottoman_era_at_their_height_.jpg/340px-Kabyle_Kingdoms_in_the_Ottoman_era_at_their_height_.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kabyle_Kingdoms_in_the_Ottoman_era_at_their_height_.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kabyle Kingdoms at their height</div></div></div>
<p>The dey was in effect a constitutional autocrat. The dey was elected for a life term, but in the 159 years (1671–1830) that the system was in place, fourteen of the twenty-nine deys were assassinated. Despite usurpation, military coups and occasional mob rule, the day-to-day operation of the Deylikal government was remarkably orderly. Although the regency patronised the tribal chieftains, it never had the unanimous allegiance of the countryside, where heavy taxation frequently provoked unrest. Autonomous tribal states were tolerated, and the regency's authority was seldom applied in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kabylie" title="Kabylie">Kabylia</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-csa16_86-3"><a href="#cite_note-csa16-86">[81]</a></sup> although in 1730 the Regency was able to take control over the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kuku" title="Kingdom of Kuku">Kingdom of Kuku</a> in western Kabylia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[99]</a></sup> Many cities in the northern parts of the Algerian desert paid taxes to Algiers or one of its Beys,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[100]</a></sup> although they otherwise retained complete autonomy from central control, while the deeper parts of the Sahara were completely independent from Algiers.
</p><p>Barbary raids in the Mediterranean continued to attack Spanish merchant shipping, and as a result, the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Navy" title="Spanish Navy">Spanish Navy</a> bombarded Algiers in <a href="/wiki/Bombardment_of_Algiers_(1783)" title="Bombardment of Algiers (1783)">1783</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bombardment_of_Algiers_(1784)" title="Bombardment of Algiers (1784)">1784</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mikaberidze_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mikaberidze-87">[82]</a></sup> For the attack in 1784, the Spanish fleet was to be joined by ships from such traditional enemies of Algiers as <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Naples" title="Kingdom of Naples">Naples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Portugal</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Knights_Hospitaller" title="Knights Hospitaller">Knights of Malta</a>. Over 20,000 cannonballs were fired, much of the city and its fortifications were destroyed and most of the Algerian fleet was sunk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[101]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Regency_of_Algiers_in_1792.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1557" data-file-width="1125" decoding="async" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Regency_of_Algiers_in_1792.jpg/170px-Regency_of_Algiers_in_1792.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Regency_of_Algiers_in_1792.jpg/255px-Regency_of_Algiers_in_1792.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Regency_of_Algiers_in_1792.jpg/340px-Regency_of_Algiers_in_1792.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Regency_of_Algiers_in_1792.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The estimated extent of the Regency of Algiers in 1792 after taking possession of the Rif and Oujda</div></div></div>
<p>In 1792, Algiers <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Siege_of_Oran_(1792)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Siege of Oran (1792) (page does not exist)">took back Oran and Mers el Kébir</a>, the two last Spanish strongholds in Algeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[102]</a></sup> In the same year, they conquered the Moroccan <a href="/wiki/Rif" title="Rif">Rif</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oujda" title="Oujda">Oujda</a>, which they then abandoned in 1795.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[103]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven,_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2061" data-file-width="2940" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven%2C_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg/220px-thumbnail.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven%2C_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg/330px-thumbnail.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven%2C_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg/440px-thumbnail.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven,_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bombardment_of_Algiers_(1816)" title="Bombardment of Algiers (1816)">Bombardment of Algiers</a> by the Anglo-Dutch fleet, to support the ultimatum to release European slaves, August 1816</div></div></div>
<p>In the 19th century, Algerian pirates forged affiliations with Caribbean powers, paying a "licence tax" in exchange for safe harbour of their vessels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[104]</a></sup>
</p><p>Attacks by Algerian pirates on <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a> merchantmen resulted in the <a href="/wiki/First_Barbary_War" title="First Barbary War">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Barbary_War" title="Second Barbary War">Second Barbary Wars</a>, which ended the attacks on U.S. ships. A year later, a combined <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">Anglo</a>-<a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="United Kingdom of the Netherlands">Dutch</a> fleet, under the command of <a href="/wiki/Edward_Pellew,_1st_Viscount_Exmouth" title="Edward Pellew, 1st Viscount Exmouth">Lord Exmouth</a> <a href="/wiki/Bombardment_of_Algiers_(1816)" title="Bombardment of Algiers (1816)">bombarded Algiers</a> to stop similar attacks on European fishermen. These efforts proved successful, although Algerian piracy would continue until the French conquest in 1830.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[105]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="French_colonization_.281830.E2.80.931962.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="French_colonization_(1830–1962)">French colonization (1830–1962)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: French colonization (1830–1962)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/French_Algeria" title="French Algeria">French Algeria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Algerian_War" title="Algerian War">Algerian War</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/French_North_Africa" title="French North Africa">French North Africa</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="662" data-file-width="702" decoding="async" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg/220px-Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg/330px-Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg/440px-Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Battle of Somah in 1836</div></div></div>
<p>Under the pretext of a slight to their consul, the French invaded and <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Algiers_in_1830" title="Invasion of Algiers in 1830">captured Algiers</a> in 1830.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[107]</a></sup> Historian <a href="/wiki/Ben_Kiernan" title="Ben Kiernan">Ben Kiernan</a> wrote on the French conquest of Algeria: "By 1875, the French conquest was complete. The war had killed approximately 825,000 indigenous Algerians since 1830."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[108]</a></sup> French losses from 1831 to 1851 were 92,329 dead in the hospital and only 3,336 killed in action.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[110]</a></sup> The population of Algeria, which stood at about 2.9 million in 1872, reached nearly 11 million in 1960.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[111]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source.
