(November 2018)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup> French policy was predicated on "civilising" the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[112]</a></sup> The slave trade and piracy in Algeria ceased following the French conquest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hannay_1911_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hannay_1911-90">[85]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/French_conquest_of_Algeria" title="French conquest of Algeria">conquest of Algeria</a> by the French took some time and resulted in considerable bloodshed. A combination of violence and disease epidemics caused the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous</a> Algerian population to decline by nearly one-third from 1830 to 1872.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ricoux1880_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ricoux1880-119">[114]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (February 2013)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup> On 17 September 1860, <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_III" title="Napoleon III">Napoleon III</a> declared "Our first duty is to take care of the happiness of the three million Arabs, whom the fate of arms has brought under our domination."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[115]</a></sup> During this time, only Kabylia resisted, the Kabylians were not colonized until after the <a href="/wiki/Mokrani_Revolt" title="Mokrani Revolt">Mokrani Revolt</a> in 1871.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Abd_al-Qadir.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="483" data-file-width="392" decoding="async" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Abd_al-Qadir.jpg/170px-Abd_al-Qadir.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Abd_al-Qadir.jpg/255px-Abd_al-Qadir.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Abd_al-Qadir.jpg/340px-Abd_al-Qadir.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Abd_al-Qadir.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abdelkader_El_Djezairi" title="Abdelkader El Djezairi">Emir Abdelkader</a>, Algerian leader insurgent against French colonial rule, 1865</div></div></div>
<p>From 1848 until independence, France administered the whole Mediterranean region of Algeria as an integral part and <i>département</i> of the nation. One of France's longest-held overseas territories, Algeria became a destination for hundreds of thousands of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_ethnic_groups" title="European ethnic groups">European</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immigrants" title="Immigrants">immigrants</a>, who became known as <i>colons</i> and later, as <i><a href="/wiki/Pied-Noir" title="Pied-Noir">Pied-Noirs</a>.</i> Between 1825 and 1847, 50,000 French people emigrated to Algeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[117]</a></sup> These settlers benefited from the French government's confiscation of communal land from tribal peoples, and the application of modern agricultural techniques that increased the amount of arable land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[118]</a></sup> Many Europeans settled in <a href="/wiki/Oran" title="Oran">Oran</a> and <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a>, and by the early 20th century they formed a majority of the population in both cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[119]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Six_chefs_FLN_-_1954.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="684" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="301" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Six_chefs_FLN_-_1954.jpg/220px-Six_chefs_FLN_-_1954.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Six_chefs_FLN_-_1954.jpg/330px-Six_chefs_FLN_-_1954.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Six_chefs_FLN_-_1954.jpg/440px-Six_chefs_FLN_-_1954.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Six_chefs_FLN_-_1954.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The six historical Leaders of the FLN: <a href="/wiki/Rabah_Bitat" title="Rabah Bitat">Rabah Bitat</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mustapha_Benboula%C3%AFd" title="Mustapha Benboulaïd">Mostefa Ben Boulaïd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Didouche_Mourad" title="Didouche Mourad">Didouche Mourad</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohammed_Boudiaf" title="Mohammed Boudiaf">Mohammed Boudiaf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krim_Belkacem" title="Krim Belkacem">Krim Belkacem</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Larbi_Ben_M%27Hidi" title="Larbi Ben M'Hidi">Larbi Ben M'Hidi</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>During the late 19th and early 20th century, the <a href="/wiki/White_Africans_of_European_ancestry" title="White Africans of European ancestry">European share</a> was almost a fifth of the population. The French government aimed at making Algeria an assimilated part of France, and this included substantial educational investments especially after 1900. The indigenous cultural and religious resistance heavily opposed this tendency, but in contrast to the other colonised countries' path in central Asia and Caucasus, Algeria kept its individual skills and a relatively human-capital intensive agriculture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[120]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>, Algeria came under <a href="/wiki/Vichy_France" title="Vichy France">Vichy control</a> before being liberated by the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allies</a> in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Torch" title="Operation Torch">Operation Torch</a>, which saw the first large-scale deployment of <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_the_United_States_during_World_War_II" title="Military history of the United States during World War II">American troops</a> in the <a href="/wiki/North_African_campaign" title="North African campaign">North African campaign</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USMA-1945_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-USMA-1945-126">[121]</a></sup>
</p><p>Gradually, dissatisfaction among the Muslim population, which lacked political and economic status under the colonial system, gave rise to demands for greater political autonomy and eventually independence from France. In May 1945, the uprising against the occupying French forces was suppressed through what is now known as the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9tif_and_Guelma_massacre" title="Sétif and Guelma massacre">Sétif and Guelma massacre</a>. Tensions between the two population groups came to a head in 1954, when the first violent events of what was later called the <a href="/wiki/Algerian_War" title="Algerian War">Algerian War</a> began after the publication of the <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_1_November_1954" title="Declaration of 1 November 1954">Declaration of 1 November 1954</a>. Historians have estimated that between 30,000 and 150,000 <a href="/wiki/Harki" title="Harki">Harkis</a> and their dependants were killed by the <a href="/wiki/National_Liberation_Front_(Algeria)" title="National Liberation Front (Algeria)">Front de Libération Nationale</a> (FLN) or by <a href="/wiki/Lynching" title="Lynching">lynch</a> mobs in Algeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[122]</a></sup> The FLN used hit and run attacks in Algeria and France as part of its war, and the French conducted <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Torture_during_the_Algerian_War_of_Independence" title="Torture during the Algerian War of Independence">severe reprisals</a>.
</p><p>The war led to the death of hundreds of thousands of Algerians and hundreds of thousands of injuries. Historians, like <a href="/wiki/Alistair_Horne" title="Alistair Horne">Alistair Horne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Aron" title="Raymond Aron">Raymond Aron</a>, state that the actual number of Algerian Muslim war dead was far greater than the original FLN and official French estimates but was less than the 1 million deaths claimed by the Algerian government after independence. Horne estimated Algerian casualties during the span of eight years to be around 700,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[123]</a></sup> The war uprooted more than 2 million Algerians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[124]</a></sup>
</p><p>The war against French rule concluded in 1962, when Algeria gained complete independence following the March 1962 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evian_agreements" title="Evian agreements">Evian agreements</a> and the July 1962 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algerian_self-determination_referendum,_1962" title="Algerian self-determination referendum, 1962">self-determination referendum</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="The_first_three_decades_of_independence_.281962.E2.80.931991.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_first_three_decades_of_independence_(1962–1991)">The first three decades of independence (1962–1991)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: The first three decades of independence (1962–1991)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Algeria_(1962%E2%80%9399)" title="History of Algeria (1962–99)">History of Algeria (1962–99)</a></div>
<p>The number of European <i><a href="/wiki/Pied-Noir" title="Pied-Noir">Pied-Noirs</a></i> who fled Algeria totaled more than 900,000 between 1962 and 1964.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[125]</a></sup> The exodus to mainland France accelerated after the <a href="/wiki/Oran_massacre_of_1962" title="Oran massacre of 1962">Oran massacre of 1962</a>, in which hundreds of militants entered European sections of the city, and began attacking civilians.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Houari_Boumediene%27s_Portrait.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="550" data-file-width="414" decoding="async" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Houari_Boumediene%27s_Portrait.jpg/140px-Houari_Boumediene%27s_Portrait.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Houari_Boumediene%27s_Portrait.jpg/210px-Houari_Boumediene%27s_Portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Houari_Boumediene%27s_Portrait.jpg/280px-Houari_Boumediene%27s_Portrait.jpg 2x" width="140"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Houari_Boumediene%27s_Portrait.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Houari_Boumediene" title="Houari Boumediene">Houari Boumediene</a></div></div></div>
<p>Algeria's first president was the Front de Libération Nationale (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FLN_(Algeria)" title="FLN (Algeria)">FLN</a>) leader <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Ben_Bella" title="Ahmed Ben Bella">Ahmed Ben Bella</a>. Morocco's claim to <a href="/wiki/Greater_Morocco" title="Greater Morocco">portions of western Algeria</a> led to the <a href="/wiki/Sand_War" title="Sand War">Sand War</a> in 1963. Ben Bella was <a href="/wiki/1965_Algerian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1965 Algerian coup d'état">overthrown in 1965</a> by <a href="/wiki/Houari_Boum%C3%A9di%C3%A8ne" title="Houari Boumédiène">Houari Boumédiène</a>, his former ally and defence minister. Under Ben Bella, the government had become increasingly socialist and <a href="/wiki/Authoritarianism" title="Authoritarianism">authoritarian</a>; Boumédienne continued this trend. But, he relied much more on the army for his support, and reduced the sole legal party to a symbolic role. He <a href="/wiki/Collective_farming" title="Collective farming">collectivised</a> agriculture and launched a massive industrialisation drive. <a href="/wiki/Extraction_of_petroleum" title="Extraction of petroleum">Oil extraction</a> facilities were nationalised. This was especially beneficial to the leadership after the international <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">1973 oil crisis</a>.
</p><p>In the 1960s and 1970s under President Houari Boumediene, Algeria pursued a program of industrialisation within a state-controlled socialist economy. Boumediene's successor, <a href="/wiki/Chadli_Bendjedid" title="Chadli Bendjedid">Chadli Bendjedid</a>, introduced some liberal economic reforms. He promoted a policy of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabisation" title="Arabisation">Arabisation</a> in Algerian society and public life. Teachers of Arabic, brought in from other Muslim countries, spread conventional Islamic thought in schools and sowed the seeds of a return to Orthodox Islam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faco_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-faco-131">[126]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Algerian economy became increasingly dependent on oil, leading to hardship when the price collapsed during the <a href="/wiki/1980s_oil_glut" title="1980s oil glut">1980s oil glut</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-132">[127]</a></sup> Economic recession caused by the crash in world oil prices resulted in Algerian social unrest during the 1980s; by the end of the decade, Bendjedid introduced a multi-party system. Political parties developed, such as the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Salvation_Front" title="Islamic Salvation Front">Islamic Salvation Front</a> (FIS), a broad coalition of Muslim groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faco_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-faco-131">[126]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Civil_War_.281991.E2.80.932002.29_and_aftermath"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_War_(1991–2002)_and_aftermath">Civil War (1991–2002) and aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Civil War (1991–2002) and aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Civil_War" title="Algerian Civil War">Algerian Civil War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Algerian_massacres_1997-1998.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="454" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Algerian_massacres_1997-1998.png/220px-Algerian_massacres_1997-1998.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Algerian_massacres_1997-1998.png/330px-Algerian_massacres_1997-1998.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Algerian_massacres_1997-1998.png/440px-Algerian_massacres_1997-1998.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Algerian_massacres_1997-1998.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/List_of_massacres_during_the_Algerian_Civil_War" title="List of massacres during the Algerian Civil War">Massacres</a> of over 50 people in 1997–1998. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armed_Islamic_Group" title="Armed Islamic Group">Armed Islamic Group (GIA)</a> claimed responsibility for many of them.</div></div></div>
<p>In December 1991 the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Salvation_Front" title="Islamic Salvation Front">Islamic Salvation Front</a> dominated the first of two rounds of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algerian_legislative_election,_1991" title="Algerian legislative election, 1991">legislative elections</a>. Fearing the election of an Islamist government, the authorities intervened on 11 January 1992, cancelling the elections. Bendjedid resigned and a <a href="/wiki/High_Council_of_State_(Algeria)" title="High Council of State (Algeria)">High Council of State</a> was installed to act as the Presidency. It banned the FIS, triggering a civil <a href="/wiki/Insurgency" title="Insurgency">insurgency</a> between the Front's armed wing, the <a href="/wiki/Armed_Islamic_Group_of_Algeria" title="Armed Islamic Group of Algeria">Armed Islamic Group</a>, and the national armed forces, in which more than 100,000 people are thought to have died. The Islamist militants conducted a violent campaign of <a href="/wiki/List_of_massacres_during_the_Algerian_Civil_War" title="List of massacres during the Algerian Civil War">civilian massacres</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[128]</a></sup> At several points in the conflict, the situation in Algeria became a point of international concern, most notably during the crisis surrounding <a href="/wiki/Air_France_Flight_8969" title="Air France Flight 8969">Air France Flight 8969</a>, a hijacking perpetrated by the Armed Islamic Group. The Armed Islamic Group declared a ceasefire in October 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faco_131-2"><a href="#cite_note-faco-131">[126]</a></sup>
</p><p>Algeria held <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algerian_presidential_election,_1999" title="Algerian presidential election, 1999">elections in 1999</a>, considered biased by international observers and most opposition groups<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[129]</a></sup> which were won by President <a href="/wiki/Abdelaziz_Bouteflika" title="Abdelaziz Bouteflika">Abdelaziz Bouteflika</a>. He worked to restore political stability to the country and announced a "Civil Concord" initiative, approved in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algerian_Civil_Concord_referendum,_1999" title="Algerian Civil Concord referendum, 1999">referendum</a>, under which many political prisoners were pardoned, and several thousand members of armed groups were granted exemption from prosecution under a limited amnesty, in force until 13 January 2000. The AIS disbanded and levels of insurgent violence fell rapidly. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Groupe_Salafiste_pour_la_Pr%C3%A9dication_et_le_Combat" title="Groupe Salafiste pour la Prédication et le Combat">Groupe Salafiste pour la Prédication et le Combat</a> (GSPC), a splinter group of the Armed Islamic Group, continued a terrorist campaign against the Government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faco_131-3"><a href="#cite_note-faco-131">[126]</a></sup>
</p><p>Bouteflika was re-elected in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algerian_presidential_election,_2004" title="Algerian presidential election, 2004">April 2004 presidential election</a> after campaigning on a programme of national reconciliation. The programme comprised economic, institutional, political and social reform to modernise the country, raise living standards, and tackle the causes of alienation. It also included a second amnesty initiative, the <a href="/wiki/Charter_for_Peace_and_National_Reconciliation" title="Charter for Peace and National Reconciliation">Charter for Peace and National Reconciliation</a>, which was approved in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algerian_national_reconciliation_referendum,_2005" title="Algerian national reconciliation referendum, 2005">referendum in September 2005</a>. It offered amnesty to most guerrillas and Government security forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faco_131-4"><a href="#cite_note-faco-131">[126]</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2008, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algerian_Constitution" title="Algerian Constitution">Algerian Constitution</a> was amended following a vote in Parliament, removing the two-term limit on Presidential incumbents. This change enabled Bouteflika to stand for re-election in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algerian_presidential_election,_2009" title="Algerian presidential election, 2009">2009 presidential elections</a>, and he was re-elected in April 2009. During his election campaign and following his re-election, Bouteflika promised to extend the programme of national reconciliation and a $150-billion spending programme to create three million new jobs, the construction of one million new housing units, and to continue public sector and infrastructure modernisation programmes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faco_131-5"><a href="#cite_note-faco-131">[126]</a></sup>
</p><p>A continuing series of protests throughout the country started on 28 December 2010, inspired by similar <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">protests across the Middle East and North Africa</a>. On 24 February 2011, the government lifted Algeria's 19-year-old <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[130]</a></sup> The government enacted legislation dealing with political parties, the electoral code, and the representation of women in elected bodies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aaeo_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-136">[131]</a></sup> In April 2011, Bouteflika promised further constitutional and political reform.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faco_131-6"><a href="#cite_note-faco-131">[126]</a></sup> However, elections are routinely criticised by opposition groups as unfair and international human rights groups say that media censorship and harassment of political opponents continue.
</p><p>On 2 April 2019, Bouteflika resigned from the presidency after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%932020_Algerian_protests" title="2019–2020 Algerian protests">mass protests</a> against his candidacy for a fifth term in office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[132]</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2019, <a href="/wiki/Abdelmadjid_Tebboune" title="Abdelmadjid Tebboune">Abdelmadjid Tebboune</a> became Algeria's president, after winning the first round of the <a href="/wiki/2019_Algerian_presidential_election" title="2019 Algerian presidential election">presidential election</a> with a record abstention rate – the highest of all presidential elections since Algeria's democracy in 1989. Tebboune is accused to be close to the military and being loyal to the deposed president. Tebboune rejects these accusations, claiming to be the victim of a witch hunt. He also reminds his detractors that he was expelled from the Government in August 2017 at the instigation of oligarchs languishing in prison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[133]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Algeria" title="Geography of Algeria">Geography of Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Algeria_relief.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="532" data-file-width="624" decoding="async" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Algeria_relief.png/220px-Algeria_relief.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Algeria_relief.png/330px-Algeria_relief.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Algeria_relief.png/440px-Algeria_relief.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Algeria_relief.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hoggar_Mountains" title="Hoggar Mountains">Hoggar Mountains</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Atlas_Mountains" title="Atlas Mountains">Atlas Mountains</a> compose the Algerian relief.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dunes.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Dunes.jpg/220px-Dunes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Dunes.jpg/330px-Dunes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/35/Dunes.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dunes.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Desert" title="Algerian Desert">Algerian Desert</a> makes up more than 90% of the country's total area.</div></div></div>
<p>Since the 2011 breakup of Sudan, and the creation of South Sudan, Algeria has been the largest country in Africa, and the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin" title="Mediterranean Basin">Mediterranean Basin</a>. Its southern part includes a significant portion of the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a>. To the north, the <a href="/wiki/Tell_Atlas" title="Tell Atlas">Tell Atlas</a> form with the <a href="/wiki/Saharan_Atlas" title="Saharan Atlas">Saharan Atlas</a>, further south, two parallel sets of reliefs in approaching eastbound, and between which are inserted vast plains and highlands. Both Atlas tend to merge in eastern Algeria. The vast mountain ranges of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aures" title="Aures">Aures</a> and <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A9bessa" title="Tébessa">Nememcha</a> occupy the entire northeastern Algeria and are delineated by the Tunisian border. The highest point is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Tahat" title="Mount Tahat">Mount Tahat</a> (3,003 metres or 9,852 feet).
</p><p>Algeria lies mostly between latitudes <a href="/wiki/19th_parallel_north" title="19th parallel north">19°</a> and <a href="/wiki/37th_parallel_north" title="37th parallel north">37°N</a> (a small area is north of 37°N and south of 19°N), and longitudes <a href="/wiki/9th_meridian_west" title="9th meridian west">9°W</a> and <a href="/wiki/12th_meridian_east" title="12th meridian east">12°E</a>. Most of the coastal area is hilly, sometimes even mountainous, and there are a few natural <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harbour" title="Harbour">harbours</a>. The area from the coast to the Tell Atlas is fertile. South of the Tell Atlas is a <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppe</a> landscape ending with the <a href="/wiki/Saharan_Atlas" title="Saharan Atlas">Saharan Atlas</a>; farther south, there is the Sahara desert.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-LOC-139">[134]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Hoggar_Mountains" title="Hoggar Mountains">Hoggar Mountains</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ar">جبال هقار</span>), also known as the Hoggar, are a highland region in central Sahara, southern Algeria. They are located about 1,500 km (932 mi) south of the capital, Algiers, and just east of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tamanghasset" title="Tamanghasset">Tamanghasset</a>. Algiers, <a href="/wiki/Oran" title="Oran">Oran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constantine,_Algeria" title="Constantine, Algeria">Constantine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Annaba" title="Annaba">Annaba</a> are Algeria's main cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_139-1"><a href="#cite_note-LOC-139">[134]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_and_hydrology">Climate and hydrology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Climate and hydrology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_of_Algeria" title="Climate of Algeria">Climate of Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_DZA_present.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="850" data-file-width="1391" decoding="async" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Koppen-Geiger_Map_DZA_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_DZA_present.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Koppen-Geiger_Map_DZA_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_DZA_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Koppen-Geiger_Map_DZA_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_DZA_present.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_DZA_present.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Algeria map of <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>In this region, midday desert temperatures can be hot year round. After sunset, however, the clear, dry air permits rapid loss of heat, and the nights are cool to chilly. Enormous daily ranges in temperature are recorded.
</p><p>Rainfall is fairly plentiful along the coastal part of the Tell Atlas, ranging from 400 to 670 mm (15.7 to 26.4 in) annually, the amount of precipitation increasing from west to east. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">Precipitation</a> is heaviest in the northern part of eastern Algeria, where it reaches as much as 1,000 mm (39.4 in) in some years.
</p><p>Farther inland, the rainfall is less plentiful. Algeria also has <a href="/wiki/Erg_(landform)" title="Erg (landform)">ergs</a>, or sand dunes, between mountains. Among these, in the summer time when winds are heavy and gusty, temperatures can go up to 43.3 °C (110 °F).
</p>
<div class="excerpt-block"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066933788">.mw-parser-output .excerpt-hat .mw-editsection-like{font-style:normal}</style><div class="excerpt">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Temperature_Bar_Chart_Africa-Algeria--1901-2020--2021-07-13.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2126" data-file-width="3780" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Temperature_Bar_Chart_Africa-Algeria--1901-2020--2021-07-13.png/220px-Temperature_Bar_Chart_Africa-Algeria--1901-2020--2021-07-13.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Temperature_Bar_Chart_Africa-Algeria--1901-2020--2021-07-13.png/330px-Temperature_Bar_Chart_Africa-Algeria--1901-2020--2021-07-13.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Temperature_Bar_Chart_Africa-Algeria--1901-2020--2021-07-13.png/440px-Temperature_Bar_Chart_Africa-Algeria--1901-2020--2021-07-13.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Temperature_Bar_Chart_Africa-Algeria--1901-2020--2021-07-13.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Temperature_anomaly" title="Temperature anomaly">Temperature anomaly</a> in Algeria, 1901 to 2020.</div></div></div>
<a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Algeria" title="Climate change in Algeria">Climate change in Algeria</a> has wide reaching effects on the country. Algeria was not a significant contributor to climate change,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Algeria_:0al_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Algeria_:0al-140">[135]</a></sup> but like <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa" title="Climate change in the Middle East and North Africa">other countries in the MENA region</a>, is expected to among the most affected by <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_climate_change" title="Effects of climate change">climate change impacts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Algeria_:1_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Algeria_:1-141">[136]</a></sup> Because a large part of the <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Algeria" title="Geography of Algeria">country is in already hot and arid geographies</a>, including part of the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a>, already strong heat and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_resource" title="Water resource">water resource</a> access challenges are expected to get worse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Algeria_:0al_140-1"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Algeria_:0al-140">[135]</a></sup> As early as 2014, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scientists" title="Scientists">scientists</a> were attributing extreme <a href="/wiki/Heat_wave" title="Heat wave">heat waves</a> to climate change in Algeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Algeria_:0al_140-2"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Algeria_:0al-140">[135]</a></sup> Algeria was ranked 46th of countries in the 2020 <a href="/wiki/Climate_Change_Performance_Index" title="Climate Change Performance Index">Climate Change Performance Index</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Algeria_:2_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Algeria_:2-142">[137]</a></sup></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna_and_flora">Fauna and flora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Fauna and flora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Algeria" title="Wildlife of Algeria">Wildlife of Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vulpes_zerda.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Vulpes_zerda.JPG/220px-Vulpes_zerda.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Vulpes_zerda.JPG/330px-Vulpes_zerda.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Vulpes_zerda.JPG/440px-Vulpes_zerda.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vulpes_zerda.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Fennec_fox" title="Fennec fox">fennec fox</a> is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_animal" title="National animal">national animal</a> of Algeria</div></div></div>
<p>The varied vegetation of Algeria includes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coastal" title="Coastal">coastal</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mountainous" title="Mountainous">mountainous</a> and grassy <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">desert</a>-like regions which all support a wide range of wildlife. Many of the creatures comprising the Algerian wildlife live in close proximity to civilisation. The most commonly seen animals include the wild <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boar" title="Boar">boars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jackal" title="Jackal">jackals</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gazelle" title="Gazelle">gazelles</a>, although it is not uncommon to spot <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fennecs" title="Fennecs">fennecs</a> (foxes), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jerboas" title="Jerboas">jerboas</a>. Algeria also has a small <a href="/wiki/African_leopard" title="African leopard">African leopard</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saharan_cheetah" title="Saharan cheetah">Saharan cheetah</a> population, but these are seldom seen. A species of deer, the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_stag" title="Barbary stag">Barbary stag</a>, inhabits the dense humid forests in the north-eastern areas. The <a href="/wiki/Fennec_fox" title="Fennec fox">fennec fox</a> is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_animal" title="National animal">national animal</a> of Algeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[138]</a></sup>
</p><p>A variety of bird species makes the country an attraction for bird watchers. The forests are inhabited by boars and jackals. <a href="/wiki/Barbary_macaque" title="Barbary macaque">Barbary macaques</a> are the sole native monkey. Snakes, <a href="/wiki/Monitor_lizard" title="Monitor lizard">monitor lizards</a>, and numerous other reptiles can be found living among an array of <a href="/wiki/Rodent" title="Rodent">rodents</a> throughout the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi_arid" title="Semi arid">semi arid</a> regions of Algeria. Many animals are now extinct, including the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_lion" title="Barbary lion">Barbary lions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlas_bear" title="Atlas bear">Atlas bears</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_African_crocodile" title="West African crocodile">crocodiles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[139]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the north, some of the native flora includes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macchia" title="Macchia">Macchia</a> scrub, <a href="/wiki/Olive" title="Olive">olive trees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">oaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cedrus" title="Cedrus">cedars</a> and other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pinophyta" title="Pinophyta">conifers</a>. The mountain regions contain large forests of evergreens (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aleppo_pine" title="Aleppo pine">Aleppo pine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juniper" title="Juniper">juniper</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evergreen_oak" title="Evergreen oak">evergreen oak</a>) and some deciduous trees. <a href="/wiki/Ficus" title="Ficus">Fig</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eucalyptus" title="Eucalyptus">eucalyptus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agave" title="Agave">agave</a>, and various <a href="/wiki/Arecaceae" title="Arecaceae">palm trees</a> grow in the warmer areas. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grape_vine" title="Grape vine">grape vine</a> is indigenous to the coast. In the Sahara region, some oases have palm trees. <a href="/wiki/Acacia" title="Acacia">Acacias</a> with wild <a href="/wiki/Olive" title="Olive">olives</a> are the predominant flora in the remainder of the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a>. Algeria had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 5.22/10, ranking it 106th globally out of 172 countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-145">[140]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Camel" title="Camel">Camels</a> are used extensively; the desert also abounds with venomous and nonvenomous snakes, <a href="/wiki/Scorpion" title="Scorpion">scorpions</a>, and numerous insects.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Algeria" title="Politics of Algeria">Politics of Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Abdelmadjid_Tebboune_20200119.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="303" data-file-width="190" decoding="async" height="271" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Abdelmadjid_Tebboune_20200119.jpg/170px-Abdelmadjid_Tebboune_20200119.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ed/Abdelmadjid_Tebboune_20200119.jpg 1.5x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Abdelmadjid_Tebboune_20200119.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Abdelmadjid_Tebboune" title="Abdelmadjid Tebboune">Abdelmadjid Tebboune</a>, President of Algeria since 2019</div></div></div>
<p>Elected politicians have relatively little sway over Algeria. Instead, a group of unelected civilian and military "décideurs" ("deciders"), known as "le pouvoir" ("the power"), actually rule the country, even deciding who should be president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[142]</a></sup> The most powerful man might have been <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Medi%C3%A8ne" title="Mohamed Mediène">Mohamed Mediène</a>, the head of military intelligence, before he was brought down during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%932020_Algerian_protests" title="2019–2020 Algerian protests">2019 protests</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[143]</a></sup> In recent years, many of these generals have died, retired, or been imprisoned. After the death of General <a href="/wiki/Larbi_Belkheir" title="Larbi Belkheir">Larbi Belkheir</a>, previous president <a href="/wiki/Bouteflika" title="Bouteflika">Bouteflika</a> put loyalists in key posts, notably at <a href="/wiki/Sonatrach" title="Sonatrach">Sonatrach</a>, and secured constitutional amendments that made him re-electable indefinitely, until he was brought down in 2019 during <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%932020_Algerian_protests" title="2019–2020 Algerian protests">protests</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[144]</a></sup>
</p><p>The head of state is the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Algeria" title="President of Algeria">President of Algeria</a>, who is elected for a five-year term. The president is limited to two five-year terms. The <a href="/wiki/2019_Algerian_presidential_election" title="2019 Algerian presidential election">most recent presidential election</a> was planned to be in April 2019, but <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2019_Algerian_protests" title="2019 Algerian protests">widespread protests</a> erupted on 22 February against the president's decision to participate in the election, which resulted in President Bouteflika announcing his resignation on 3 April.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[145]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Abdelmadjid_Tebboune" title="Abdelmadjid Tebboune">Abdelmadjid Tebboune</a>, an independent candidate, was elected as president after the election eventually took place on 12 December 2019. Protestors refused to recognise Tebboune as president, citing demands for comprehensive reform of the political system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[146]</a></sup> Algeria has universal <a href="/wiki/Suffrage" title="Suffrage">suffrage</a> at 18 years of age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-3">[3]</a></sup> The President is the head of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algerian_Army" title="Algerian Army">army</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_of_Algeria" title="Council of Ministers of Algeria">Council of Ministers</a> and the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=High_Security_Council&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="High Security Council (page does not exist)">High Security Council</a>. He appoints the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Algeria" title="Prime Minister of Algeria">Prime Minister</a> who is also the head of government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-president_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-president-152">[147]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_(Alg%C3%A9rie).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2720" data-file-width="4080" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg/220px-H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg/330px-H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg/440px-H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_(Alg%C3%A9rie).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/People%27s_National_Assembly" title="People's National Assembly">People's National Assembly</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Algerian parliament is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicameral" title="Bicameral">bicameral</a>; the lower house, the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_National_Assembly" title="People's National Assembly">People's National Assembly</a>, has 462 members who are directly elected for five-year terms, while the upper house, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_Nation" title="Council of the Nation">Council of the Nation</a>, has 144 members serving six-year terms, of which 96 members are chosen by local assemblies and 48 are appointed by the president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fitw13_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-fitw13-153">[148]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Algeria" title="Constitution of Algeria">constitution</a>, no political association may be formed if it is "based on differences in religion, language, race, gender, profession, or region". In addition, political campaigns must be exempt from the aforementioned subjects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[149]</a></sup>
</p><p>Parliamentary elections were last held in <a href="/wiki/2017_Algerian_legislative_election" title="2017 Algerian legislative election">May 2017</a>. In the elections, the <a href="/wiki/National_Liberation_Front_(Algeria)" title="National Liberation Front (Algeria)">FLN</a> lost 44 of its seats, but remained the largest party with 164 seats, the military-backed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Rally_for_Democracy_(Algeria)" title="National Rally for Democracy (Algeria)">National Rally for Democracy</a> won 100, and the Muslim Brotherhood-linked <a href="/wiki/Movement_of_Society_for_Peace" title="Movement of Society for Peace">Movement of the Society for Peace</a> won 33.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[150]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Algeria" title="Foreign relations of Algeria">Foreign relations of Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="350" data-file-width="514" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg/220px-Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg/330px-Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg/440px-Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Abdelaziz_Bouteflika" title="Abdelaziz Bouteflika">Abdelaziz Bouteflika</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> exchange handshakes at the Windsor Hotel Toya Resort and Spa in Tōyako Town, Abuta District, Hokkaidō in 2008. With them are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dmitriy_Medvedev" title="Dmitriy Medvedev">Dmitriy Medvedev</a>, left, and <a href="/wiki/Yasuo_Fukuda" title="Yasuo Fukuda">Yasuo Fukuda</a>, right.</div></div></div>
<p>Algeria is included in the European Union's <a href="/wiki/European_Neighbourhood_Policy" title="European Neighbourhood Policy">European Neighbourhood Policy</a> (ENP) which aims at bringing the EU and its neighbours closer.
Giving incentives and rewarding best performers, as well as offering funds in a faster and more flexible manner, are the two main principles underlying the European Neighbourhood Instrument (ENI) that came into force in 2014. It has a budget of €15.4 billion and provides the bulk of funding through a number of programmes.
</p><p>In 2009, the French government agreed to compensate victims of nuclear tests in Algeria. Defence Minister Herve Morin stated that "It's time for our country to be at peace with itself, at peace thanks to a system of compensation and reparations," when presenting the draft law on the payouts. Algerian officials and activists believe that this is a good first step and hope that this move would encourage broader reparation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[151]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Algeria%E2%80%93Morocco_relations" title="Algeria–Morocco relations">Tensions between Algeria and Morocco</a> in relation to the <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a> have been an obstacle to tightening the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Maghreb_Union" title="Arab Maghreb Union">Arab Maghreb Union</a>, nominally established in 1989, but which has carried little practical weight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[152]</a></sup> On 24 August 2021, Algeria announced the break of diplomatic relations with Morocco.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[153]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Algeria" title="Military of Algeria">Military of Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Al-chihab.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="496" data-file-width="913" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Al-chihab.jpg/220px-Al-chihab.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Al-chihab.jpg/330px-Al-chihab.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Al-chihab.jpg/440px-Al-chihab.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Al-chihab.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Djebel_Chenoua-class_corvette" title="Djebel Chenoua-class corvette"><i>Djebel Chenoua</i>-class corvette</a>, designed and assembled in Algeria</div></div></div>
<p>The military of Algeria consists of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_National_Army" title="People's National Army">People's National Army</a> (ANP), the <a href="/wiki/Algerian_National_Navy" title="Algerian National Navy">Algerian National Navy</a> (MRA), and the <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Air_Force" title="Algerian Air Force">Algerian Air Force</a> (QJJ), plus the <a href="/wiki/Territorial_Air_Defence_Forces" title="Territorial Air Defence Forces">Territorial Air Defence Forces</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-159">[154]</a></sup> It is the direct successor of the <a href="/wiki/National_Liberation_Army_(Algeria)" title="National Liberation Army (Algeria)">National Liberation Army</a> (Armée de Libération Nationale or ALN), the armed wing of the nationalist National Liberation Front which fought French colonial <a href="/wiki/Military_occupation" title="Military occupation">occupation</a> during the Algerian War of Independence (1954–62).
</p><p>Total military personnel include 147,000 active, 150,000 reserve, and 187,000 paramilitary staff (2008 estimate).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IISS_TMB_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-IISS_TMB-160">[155]</a></sup> Service in the military is compulsory for men aged 19–30, for a total of 12 months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[156]</a></sup> The military expenditure was 4.3% of the <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP) in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_159-1"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-159">[154]</a></sup> Algeria has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_military_and_paramilitary_personnel" title="List of countries by number of military and paramilitary personnel">second largest military</a> in North Africa with the largest defence budget in Africa ($10 billion).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaSpending_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaSpending-162">[157]</a></sup> Most of Algeria's weapons are imported from <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, with whom they <a href="/wiki/Algeria%E2%80%93Russia_relations" title="Algeria–Russia relations">are a close ally</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaSpending_162-1"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaSpending-162">[157]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[158]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007, the Algerian Air Force signed a deal with Russia to purchase 49 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MiG-29" title="MiG-29">MiG-29</a>SMT and 6 MiG-29UBT at an estimated cost of $1.9 billion. Russia is also building two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kilo_class_submarine" title="Kilo class submarine">636-type</a> diesel <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Submarines" title="Submarines">submarines</a> for Algeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[159]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Algeria" title="Human rights in Algeria">Human rights in Algeria</a></div>
<p>Algeria has been categorised by the US government funded <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> as "not free" since it began publishing such ratings in 1972, with the exception of 1989, 1990, and 1991, when the country was labelled "partly free."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[160]</a></sup> In December 2016, the <i>Euro-Mediterranean Human Rights Monitor</i> issued a report regarding violation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Media_freedom" title="Media freedom">media freedom</a> in Algeria. It clarified that the Algerian government imposed restrictions on <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press" title="Freedom of the press">freedom of the press</a>; expression; and right to peaceful demonstration, protest and assembly as well as intensified censorship of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadcast_media" title="Broadcast media">media</a> and websites. Due to the fact that the journalists and activists criticise the ruling government, some media organisations' licenses are cancelled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[161]</a></sup>
</p><p>Independent and autonomous trade unions face routine harassment from the government, with many leaders imprisoned and protests suppressed. In 2016, a number of unions, many of which were involved in the 2010–2012 Algerian Protests, have been deregistered by the government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[162]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[163]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[164]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Algeria" title="LGBT rights in Algeria">Homosexuality</a> is illegal in Algeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[165]</a></sup> Public homosexual behavior is punishable by up to two years in prison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[166]</a></sup> Despite this, about 26% of Algerians think that homosexuality should be accepted, according to the survey conducted by the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Arabic" title="BBC Arabic">BBC News Arabic</a>-Arab Barometer in 2019. Algeria showed largest LGBT acceptance compared to other Arab countries where the survey was conducted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[167]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> has accused the Algerian authorities of using the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> as an excuse to prevent pro-democracy movements and protests in the country, leading to the arrest of youths as part of <a href="/wiki/Social_distancing" title="Social distancing">social distancing</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[168]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Algeria" title="Provinces of Algeria">Provinces of Algeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Algeria" title="Districts of Algeria">Districts of Algeria</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Algeria" title="Municipalities of Algeria">Municipalities of Algeria</a></div>
<p>Algeria is divided into 58 <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Algeria" title="Provinces of Algeria">provinces</a> (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wilaya" title="Wilaya">wilayas</a></i>), 553 <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Algeria" title="Districts of Algeria">districts</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Da%C3%AFra" title="Daïra">daïras</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[169]</a></sup> and 1,541 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Algeria" title="Municipalities of Algeria">municipalities</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Baladiyah" title="Baladiyah">baladiyahs</a></i>). Each province, district, and municipality is named after its <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">seat</a>, which is usually the largest city.
</p><p>The administrative divisions have changed several times since independence. When introducing new provinces, the numbers of old provinces are kept, hence the non-alphabetical order. With their official numbers, currently (since 1983) they are<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_159-2"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-159">[154]</a></sup>
</p>
