<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Algeria" title="Economy of Algeria">Economy of Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GDP_per_capita_development_in_Algeria.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="657" data-file-width="1025" decoding="async" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/GDP_per_capita_development_in_Algeria.png/300px-GDP_per_capita_development_in_Algeria.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/GDP_per_capita_development_in_Algeria.png/450px-GDP_per_capita_development_in_Algeria.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/GDP_per_capita_development_in_Algeria.png/600px-GDP_per_capita_development_in_Algeria.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GDP_per_capita_development_in_Algeria.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>GDP per capita development in Algeria</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Algeria_Product_Exports_(2019).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="715" data-file-width="1100" decoding="async" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Algeria_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg/300px-Algeria_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Algeria_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg/450px-Algeria_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Algeria_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg/600px-Algeria_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Algeria_Product_Exports_(2019).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A proportional representation of Algeria exports, 2019</div></div></div>
<p>Algeria's currency is the <a href="/wiki/Algerian_dinar" title="Algerian dinar">dinar</a> (DZD). The economy remains dominated by the state, a legacy of the country's socialist post-independence development model. In recent years, the Algerian government has halted the privatization of state-owned industries and imposed restrictions on imports and foreign involvement in its economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_159-3"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-159">[154]</a></sup> These restrictions are just starting to be lifted off recently although questions about Algeria's slowly-diversifying economy remain.
</p><p>Algeria has struggled to develop industries outside hydrocarbons in part because of high costs and an inert state bureaucracy. The government's efforts to diversify the economy by attracting foreign and domestic investment outside the energy sector have done little to reduce high youth unemployment rates or to address housing shortages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_159-4"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-159">[154]</a></sup> The country is facing a number of short-term and medium-term problems, including the need to diversify the economy, strengthen political, economic and financial reforms, improve the business climate and reduce inequalities amongst regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aaeo_136-1"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-136">[131]</a></sup>
</p><p>A wave of economic protests in February and March 2011 prompted the Algerian government to offer more than $23 billion in public grants and retroactive salary and benefit increases. Public spending has increased by 27% annually during the past 5 years. The 2010–14 public-investment programme will cost US$286 billion, 40% of which will go to human development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aaeo_136-2"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-136">[131]</a></sup>
</p><p>Thanks to strong hydrocarbon revenues, Algeria has a cushion of $173 billion in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foreign_currency_reserves" title="Foreign currency reserves">foreign currency reserves</a> and a large hydrocarbon stabilisation fund. In addition, Algeria's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_external_debt" title="List of countries by external debt">external debt</a> is extremely low at about 2% of GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_159-5"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-159">[154]</a></sup> The economy remains very dependent on hydrocarbon wealth, and, despite high foreign exchange reserves (US$178 billion, equivalent to three years of imports), current expenditure growth makes Algeria's budget more vulnerable to the risk of prolonged lower hydrocarbon revenues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imfart4_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-imfart4-175">[170]</a></sup>
</p><p>Algeria has not joined the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WTO" title="WTO">WTO</a>, despite several years of negotiations but is a member of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Arab_Free_Trade_Area" title="Greater Arab Free Trade Area">Greater Arab Free Trade Area</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[171]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/African_Continental_Free_Trade_Area" title="African Continental Free Trade Area">African Continental Free Trade Area</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[172]</a></sup> and has an association agreement with the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[173]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[174]</a></sup>
</p><p>Turkish direct investments have accelerated in Algeria, with total value reaching $5 billion. As of 2022, the number of Turkish companies present in Algeria has reached 1,400. In 2020, despite the pandemic, more than 130 Turkish companies were created in Algeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[175]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oil_and_natural_resources">Oil and natural resources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Oil and natural resources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mining_industry_of_Algeria" title="Mining industry of Algeria">Mining industry of Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="799" data-file-width="832" decoding="async" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg/220px-Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg/330px-Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg/440px-Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pipelines across Algeria</div></div></div>
<p>Algeria, whose economy is reliant on petroleum, has been an <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a> member since 1969. Its crude oil production stands at around 1.1 million barrels/day, but it is also a major gas producer and exporter, with important links to Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opb15_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-opb15-181">[176]</a></sup> Hydrocarbons have long been the backbone of the economy, accounting for roughly 60% of budget revenues, 30% of GDP, and 87.7%<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[177]</a></sup> of export earnings. Algeria has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_gas_proven_reserves" title="List of countries by natural gas proven reserves">10th-largest reserves of natural gas</a> in the world and is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_gas_exports" title="List of countries by natural gas exports">sixth-largest gas exporter</a>. The U.S. <a href="/wiki/Energy_Information_Administration" title="Energy Information Administration">Energy Information Administration</a> reported that in 2005, Algeria had 4.5 trillion cubic metres (160<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>12</sup> cu ft) of proven <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natural_gas_reserves" title="Natural gas reserves">natural-gas reserves</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ciawfb_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-ciawfb-183">[178]</a></sup> It also ranks <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_proven_oil_reserves" title="List of countries by proven oil reserves">16th in oil reserves</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_159-6"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-159">[154]</a></sup>
</p><p>Non-hydrocarbon growth for 2011 was projected at 5%. To cope with social demands, the authorities raised expenditure, especially on basic food support, employment creation, support for SMEs, and higher salaries. High hydrocarbon prices have improved the current account and the already large international reserves position.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imfart4_175-1"><a href="#cite_note-imfart4-175">[170]</a></sup>
</p><p>Income from oil and gas rose in 2011 as a result of continuing high oil prices, though the trend in production volume is downwards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aaeo_136-3"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-136">[131]</a></sup> Production from the oil and gas sector in terms of volume, continues to decline, dropping from 43.2 million tonnes to 32 million tonnes between 2007 and 2011. Nevertheless, the sector accounted for 98% of the total volume of exports in 2011, against 48% in 1962,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[179]</a></sup> and 70% of budgetary receipts, or US$71.4 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aaeo_136-4"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-136">[131]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Algerian national oil company is <a href="/wiki/Sonatrach" title="Sonatrach">Sonatrach</a>, which plays a key role in all aspects of the oil and natural gas sectors in Algeria. All foreign operators must work in partnership with Sonatrach, which usually has majority ownership in production-sharing agreements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[180]</a></sup>
</p><p>Access to <a href="/wiki/Biocapacity" title="Biocapacity">biocapacity</a> in Algeria is lower than world average. In 2016, Algeria had 0.53 global hectares<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-footprintdata_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-footprintdata-186">[181]</a></sup> of biocapacity per person within its territory, much less than the world average of 1.6 global hectares per person.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[182]</a></sup> In 2016, Algeria used 2.4 global hectares of biocapacity per person – their <a href="/wiki/Ecological_footprint" title="Ecological footprint">ecological footprint</a> of consumption. This means they use just under 4.5 times as much biocapacity as Algeria contains. As a result, Algeria is running a biocapacity deficit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-footprintdata_186-1"><a href="#cite_note-footprintdata-186">[181]</a></sup> In April 2022, diplomats from <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> held talks after Rome's move to secure large volume of Algerian gas stoked concerns in Madrid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[183]</a></sup> Under the deal between Algeria's Sonatrach and Italy's Eni, Algeria will send an additional 9 billion cubic metres of gas to Italy by next year and in 2024.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[184]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_and_alternative_energy_sources">Research and alternative energy sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Research and alternative energy sources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Algeria has invested an estimated 100 billion dinars towards developing research facilities and paying researchers. This development program is meant to advance alternative energy production, especially solar and wind power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[185]</a></sup> Algeria is estimated to have the largest solar energy potential in the Mediterranean, so the government has funded the creation of a solar science park in Hassi R'Mel. Currently, Algeria has 20,000 research professors at various universities and over 780 research labs, with state-set goals to expand to 1,000. Besides solar energy, areas of research in Algeria include space and satellite telecommunications, nuclear power and medical research.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Labour_market">Labour market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Labour market">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The overall rate of unemployment was 10% in 2011, but remained higher among young people, with a rate of 21.5% for those aged between 15 and 24. The government strengthened in 2011 the job programs introduced in 1988, in particular in the framework of the program to aid those seeking work (Dispositif d'Aide à l'Insertion Professionnelle).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aaeo_136-5"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-136">[131]</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite a decline in total <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment</a>, youth and women unemployment is high.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imfart4_175-2"><a href="#cite_note-imfart4-175">[170]</a></sup> Unemployment particularly affects the young, with a jobless rate of 21.5% among the 15–24 age group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aaeo_136-6"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-136">[131]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Algeria" title="Tourism in Algeria">Tourism in Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2981" data-file-width="4500" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg/220px-Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg/330px-Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg/440px-Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Djanet" title="Djanet">Djanet</a></div></div></div>
<p>The development of the tourism sector in Algeria had previously been hampered by a lack of facilities, but since 2004 a broad tourism development strategy has been implemented resulting in many hotels of a high modern standard being built.
</p><p>There are several <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Sites" title="World Heritage Sites">World Heritage Sites</a> in Algeria<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[186]</a></sup> including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al_Qal%27a_of_Beni_Hammad" title="Al Qal'a of Beni Hammad">Al Qal'a of Beni Hammad</a>, the first capital of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hammadid" title="Hammadid">Hammadid</a> empire; <a href="/wiki/Tipasa" title="Tipasa">Tipasa</a>, a Phoenician and later Roman town; and <a href="/wiki/Dj%C3%A9mila" title="Djémila">Djémila</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timgad" title="Timgad">Timgad</a>, both <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Roman</a> ruins; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M%27Zab_Valley" title="M'Zab Valley">M'Zab Valley</a>, a limestone valley containing a large urbanized <a href="/wiki/Oasis" title="Oasis">oasis</a>; and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Casbah" title="Casbah">Casbah</a> of Algiers, an important citadel. The only natural <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Tassili_n%27Ajjer" title="Tassili n'Ajjer">Tassili n'Ajjer</a>, a mountain range.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Algeria" title="Transport in Algeria">Transport in Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="808" data-file-width="1528" decoding="async" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG/220px-Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG/330px-Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG/440px-Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The main highway connecting the Moroccan to the Tunisian border was a part of the <a href="/wiki/Cairo%E2%80%93Dakar_Highway" title="Cairo–Dakar Highway">Cairo–Dakar Highway</a> project</div></div></div>
<p>The Algerian road network is the densest in Africa; its length is estimated at 180,000 km (110,000 mi) of highways, with more than 3,756 structures and a paving rate of 85%. This network will be complemented by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algeria_East%E2%80%93West_Highway" title="Algeria East–West Highway">East-West Highway</a>, a major infrastructure project currently under construction. It is a 3-way, 1,216-kilometre-long (756 mi) highway, linking <a href="/wiki/Annaba" title="Annaba">Annaba</a> in the extreme east to the <a href="/wiki/Tlemcen" title="Tlemcen">Tlemcen</a> in the far west. Algeria is also crossed by the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Sahara_Highway" title="Trans-Sahara Highway">Trans-Sahara Highway</a>, which is now completely paved. This road is supported by the Algerian government to increase trade between the six countries crossed: Algeria, <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Algeria" title="Demographics of Algeria">Demographics of Algeria</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Algeria" title="List of cities in Algeria">List of cities in Algeria</a></div>
<p>Algeria has a population of an estimated 44 million, of which the vast majority are <a href="/wiki/Arab-Berber" title="Arab-Berber">Arab-Berber</a> ethnically.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_159-7"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-159">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ons_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-ons-192">[187]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ber_evidance_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-ber_evidance-193">[188]</a></sup> At the outset of the 20th century, its population was approximately four million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[189]</a></sup> About 90% of Algerians live in the northern, coastal area; the inhabitants of the Sahara desert are mainly concentrated in <a href="/wiki/Oasis" title="Oasis">oases</a>, although some 1.5 million remain <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomadic</a> or partly nomadic. 28.1% of Algerians are under the age of 15.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_159-8"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-159">[154]</a></sup>
</p><p>Between 90,000 and 165,000 <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_people" title="Sahrawi people">Sahrawis</a> from <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a> live in the <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_refugee_camps" title="Sahrawi refugee camps">Sahrawi refugee camps</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNHCRAlgeria_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCRAlgeria-195">[190]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USCRIAlgeria_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-USCRIAlgeria-196">[191]</a></sup> in the western Algerian Sahara desert.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[192]</a></sup> There are also more than 4,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_refugee" title="Palestinian refugee">Palestinian refugees</a>, who are well integrated and have not asked for assistance from the United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees (UNHCR).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNHCRAlgeria_195-1"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCRAlgeria-195">[190]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USCRIAlgeria_196-1"><a href="#cite_note-USCRIAlgeria-196">[191]</a></sup> In 2009, 35,000 <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Chinese</a> migrant workers lived in Algeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[193]</a></sup>
</p><p>The largest concentration of Algerian migrants outside Algeria is in France, which has reportedly over 1.7 million <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algerians" title="Algerians">Algerians</a> of up to the second generation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[194]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Algeria" title="Ethnic groups in Algeria">Ethnic groups in Algeria</a></div>
<p>Indigenous <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">Berbers</a> as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phoenicians" title="Phoenicians">Phoenicians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">Vandals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Greeks" title="Byzantine Greeks">Byzantine Greeks</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab_people" title="Arab people">Arabs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turks</a>, various <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africans" title="Sub-Saharan Africans">Sub-Saharan Africans</a>, and <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">French</a> have contributed to the history of Algeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[195]</a></sup> Descendants of <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Andalusian</a> refugees are also present in the population of Algiers and other cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[196]</a></sup> Moreover, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> was spoken by these <a href="/wiki/Aragon" title="Aragon">Aragonese</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Castilian_people" title="Castilian people">Castillian</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moriscos" title="Moriscos">Morisco</a> descendants deep into the 18th century, and even <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a> was spoken at the same time by <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalan</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moriscos" title="Moriscos">Morisco</a> descendants in the small town of Grish El-Oued.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[197]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="263" data-file-width="454" decoding="async" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png/220px-Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png/330px-Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png/440px-Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Some of Algeria's traditional clothes</div></div></div>
<p>Despite the dominance of the Berber ethnicity in Algeria, the majority of Algerians identify with an Arabic-based identity, especially after the Arab nationalism rising in the 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[198]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag relies on an unreliable source. The Encyclopedia doesn't show a source or a statistical effort for the claim that the overwhelming majority of population is bebrer. This claim is widely controversial and should be sourced from a serious place with actual studies. (June 2021)">unreliable source</span></a></i>]</sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[199]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="Quotation needed from source to verify. (June 2021)">need quotation to verify</span></a></i>]</sup> Berbers and Berber-speaking Algerians are divided into many groups with varying languages. The largest of these are the Kabyles, who live in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kabylie" title="Kabylie">Kabylie</a> region east of Algiers, the Chaoui of Northeast Algeria, the Tuaregs in the southern desert and the <a href="/wiki/Chenouas" title="Chenouas">Shenwa people</a> of North Algeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[200]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (February 2013)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>During the colonial period, there was a large (10% in 1960)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cook_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cook-206">[201]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">European</a> population who became known as <i><a href="/wiki/Pied-Noir" title="Pied-Noir">Pied-Noirs</a></i>. They were primarily of French, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_people" title="Spanish people">Spanish</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_people" title="Italian people">Italian</a> origin. Almost all of this population left during the war of independence or immediately after its end.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[202]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Algeria" title="Languages of Algeria">Languages of Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg/220px-Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg/330px-Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg/440px-Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Signs in the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Tizi_Ouzou" title="University of Tizi Ouzou">University of Tizi Ouzou</a> in three languages: <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">Berber</a>, and French</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Modern_Standard_Arabic" title="Modern Standard Arabic">Modern Standard Arabic</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berber_language" title="Berber language">Berber</a> are the official languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitution_of_Algeria_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution_of_Algeria-208">[203]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Arabic" title="Algerian Arabic">Algerian Arabic</a> (Darja) is the language used by the majority of the population. Colloquial Algerian Arabic is heavily infused with borrowings from French and Berber.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berber_language" title="Berber language">Berber</a> has been recognised as a "national language" by the constitutional amendment of 8 May 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[204]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kabyle_language" title="Kabyle language">Kabyle</a>, the predominant Berber language, is taught and is partially co-official (with a few restrictions) in parts of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kabylie" title="Kabylie">Kabylie</a>. In February 2016, the Algerian constitution passed a resolution that made Berber an official language alongside Arabic.
</p><p>Although <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> has no official status in Algeria, it has one of the largest Francophone populations in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[205]</a></sup> and French is widely used in government, media (newspapers, radio, local television), and both the education system (from primary school onwards) and academia due to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_rule_in_Algeria" title="French rule in Algeria">Algeria's colonial history</a>. It can be regarded as a <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> of Algeria. In 2008, 11.2 million Algerians could read and write in French.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[206]</a></sup> An Abassa Institute study in April 2000 found that 60% of households could speak and understand French, or 18 million people out of a total of 30 million at the time. Following a period during which the Algerian government tried to phase out French, in recent decades the government has changed course and reinforced the study of French, and some television programs are broadcast in the language.
</p><p>Algeria emerged as a bilingual state after 1962.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[207]</a></sup> Colloquial <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Arabic" title="Algerian Arabic">Algerian Arabic</a> is spoken by about 72% of the population and Berber by 27–30%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leclerc_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-leclerc-213">[208]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Algeria" title="Religion in Algeria">Religion in Algeria</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Algeria" title="Islam in Algeria">Islam in Algeria</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Early_African_Church" title="Early African Church">Early African Church</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Algeria" title="History of the Jews in Algeria">History of the Jews in Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mosque_Hassan_Pacha_Oran_1790_(6).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2976" data-file-width="2976" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Mosque_Hassan_Pacha_Oran_1790_%286%29.jpg/220px-Mosque_Hassan_Pacha_Oran_1790_%286%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Mosque_Hassan_Pacha_Oran_1790_%286%29.jpg/330px-Mosque_Hassan_Pacha_Oran_1790_%286%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Mosque_Hassan_Pacha_Oran_1790_%286%29.jpg/440px-Mosque_Hassan_Pacha_Oran_1790_%286%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mosque_Hassan_Pacha_Oran_1790_(6).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hassan_Pasha_Mosque" title="Hassan Pasha Mosque">Hassan Pasha Mosque</a> in <a href="/wiki/Oran" title="Oran">Oran</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> is the predominant religion in Algeria, with its adherents, mostly Sunnis, accounting for 99% of the population according to a 2021 CIA <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Factbook" title="World Factbook">World Factbook</a></i> estimate,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_159-9"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-159">[154]</a></sup> and 97.9% according to Pew Research in 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pew_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-pew-214">[209]</a></sup> There are about 290,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ibadi" title="Ibadi">Ibadis</a> in the M'zab Valley in the region of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ghardaia" title="Ghardaia">Ghardaia</a>. Estimates of the <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Algeria" title="Christianity in Algeria">Christian population</a> range from 20,000 to 200,000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-215">[210]</a></sup> Algerian citizens who are Christians predominantly belong to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> groups, which have seen increased pressure from the government in recent years including many forced closures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_215-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-215">[210]</a></sup>
</p><p>There has been an increase in the number of people identifying as non-religious. The June 2019 <a href="/wiki/Arab_Barometer" title="Arab Barometer">Arab Barometer</a>-<a href="/wiki/BBC_News" title="BBC News">BBC News</a> report found that the percentage of Algerians identifying as non-religious has grown from around 8% in 2013 to around 15% in 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[211]</a></sup> The Arab Barometer December 2019, found that the growth in the percentage of Algerians identifying as non-religious is largely driven by young Algerians, with roughly 25% describing themselves as non-religious.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[212]</a></sup>
</p><p>Algeria has given the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_world" title="Muslim world">Muslim world</a> a number of prominent thinkers, including <a href="/wiki/Emir_Abdelkader" title="Emir Abdelkader">Emir Abdelkader</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abdelhamid_Ben_Badis" title="Abdelhamid Ben Badis">Abdelhamid Ben Badis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mouloud_Kacem_Na%C3%AEt_Belkacem" title="Mouloud Kacem Naît Belkacem">Mouloud Kacem Naît Belkacem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malek_Bennabi" title="Malek Bennabi">Malek Bennabi</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohamed_Arkoun" title="Mohamed Arkoun">Mohamed Arkoun</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Algeria" title="Health in Algeria">Health in Algeria</a></div>
<p>In 2018, Algeria had the highest numbers of physicians in the Maghreb region (1.72 per 1,000 people), nurses (2.23 per 1,000 people), and dentists (0.31 per 1,000 people). Access to "improved water sources" was around 97.4% of the population in urban areas and 98.7% of the population in the rural areas. Some 99% of Algerians living in urban areas, and around 93.4% of those living in rural areas, had access to "improved sanitation". According to the World Bank, Algeria is making progress toward its goal of "reducing by half the number of people without sustainable access to improved drinking water and basic sanitation by 2015". Given Algeria's young population, policy favours preventive health care and clinics over hospitals. In keeping with this policy, the government maintains an immunisation program. However, poor sanitation and unclean water still cause <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hepatitis" title="Hepatitis">hepatitis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">measles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Typhoid_fever" title="Typhoid fever">typhoid fever</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dysentery" title="Dysentery">dysentery</a>. The poor generally receive health care free of charge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[213]</a></sup>
</p><p>Health records have been maintained in Algeria since 1882 and began adding Muslims living in the south to their vital record database in 1905 during French rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[214]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Algeria" title="Education in Algeria">Education in Algeria</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Algeria" title="List of universities in Algeria">List of universities in Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UIS_Literacy_Rate_Algeria_population_plus15_1980_2015.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="314" data-file-width="397" decoding="async" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/UIS_Literacy_Rate_Algeria_population_plus15_1980_2015.png/220px-UIS_Literacy_Rate_Algeria_population_plus15_1980_2015.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/UIS_Literacy_Rate_Algeria_population_plus15_1980_2015.png/330px-UIS_Literacy_Rate_Algeria_population_plus15_1980_2015.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/14/UIS_Literacy_Rate_Algeria_population_plus15_1980_2015.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UIS_Literacy_Rate_Algeria_population_plus15_1980_2015.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Institute_for_Statistics" title="UNESCO Institute for Statistics">UIS</a> literacy rate Algeria population plus 15 1985–2015</div></div></div>
<p>Since the 1970s, in a centralised system that was designed to significantly reduce the rate of illiteracy, the Algerian government introduced a decree by which school attendance became compulsory for all children aged between 6 and 15 years who have the ability to track their learning through the 20 facilities built since independence, now the literacy rate is around 92.6%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-APSLIT_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-APSLIT-220">[215]</a></sup> Since 1972, Arabic is used as the language of instruction during the first nine years of schooling. From the third year, French is taught and it is also the language of instruction for science classes. The students can also learn English, Italian, Spanish and German. In 2008, new programs at the elementary appeared, therefore the compulsory schooling does not start at the age of six anymore, but at the age of five.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[216]</a></sup> Apart from the 122 private schools, the Universities of the State are free of charge. After nine years of primary school, students can go to the high school or to an educational institution. The school offers two programs: general or technical. At the end of the third year of secondary school, students pass the exam of the baccalaureate, which allows once it is successful to pursue graduate studies in universities and institutes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[217]</a></sup>
</p><p>Education is officially compulsory for children between the ages of six and 15. In 2008, the illiteracy rate for people over 10 was 22.3%, 15.6% for men and 29.0% for women. The province with the lowest rate of illiteracy was <a href="/wiki/Algiers_Province" title="Algiers Province">Algiers Province</a> at 11.6%, while the province with the highest rate was <a href="/wiki/Djelfa_Province" title="Djelfa Province">Djelfa Province</a> at 35.5%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-illit_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-illit-223">[218]</a></sup>
</p><p>Algeria has 26 universities and 67 institutions of higher education, which must accommodate a million Algerians and 80,000 foreign students in 2008. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Algiers" title="University of Algiers">University of Algiers</a>, founded in 1879, is the oldest, it offers education in various disciplines (law, medicine, science and letters). Twenty-five of these universities and almost all of the institutions of higher education were founded after the independence of the country.
</p><p>Even if some of them offer instruction in <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a> like areas of law and the economy, most of the other sectors as science and medicine continue to be provided in French and English. Among the most important universities, there are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Sciences_and_Technology_Houari_Boumediene" title="University of Sciences and Technology Houari Boumediene">University of Sciences and Technology Houari Boumediene</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Mentouri" title="University of Mentouri">University of Mentouri</a> Constantine, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Oran" title="University of Oran">University of Oran</a> Es-Senia. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Abou_Bekr_Belka%C3%AFd" title="University of Abou Bekr Belkaïd">University of Abou Bekr Belkaïd</a> in Tlemcen and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Batna" title="University of Batna">University of Batna</a> Hadj Lakhdar occupy the 26th and 45th row in Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[219]</a></sup> Algeria was ranked 120th in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Innovation_Index" title="Global Innovation Index">Global Innovation Index</a> in 2021, down from 113rd in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[220]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[221]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[222]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[223]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Algeria" title="Culture of Algeria">Culture of Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bensari2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1189" data-file-width="1724" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Bensari2.jpg/220px-Bensari2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Bensari2.jpg/330px-Bensari2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Bensari2.jpg/440px-Bensari2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bensari2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Algerian musicians in <a href="/wiki/Tlemcen" title="Tlemcen">Tlemcen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Algeria" title="Ottoman Algeria">Ottoman Algeria</a>; by <a href="/wiki/Bachir_Yell%C3%A8s" title="Bachir Yellès">Bachir Yellès</a></div></div></div>
<p>Modern Algerian literature, split between <a href="/wiki/Classical_Arabic" title="Classical Arabic">Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">Tamazight</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Language" title="French Language">French</a>, has been strongly influenced by the country's recent history. <a href="/wiki/List_of_Algerian_writers" title="List of Algerian writers">Famous novelists</a> of the 20th century include <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Dib" title="Mohammed Dib">Mohammed Dib</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Camus" title="Albert Camus">Albert Camus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kateb_Yacine" title="Kateb Yacine">Kateb Yacine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ahlam_Mosteghanemi" title="Ahlam Mosteghanemi">Ahlam Mosteghanemi</a> while <a href="/wiki/Assia_Djebar" title="Assia Djebar">Assia Djebar</a> is widely translated. Among the important novelists of the 1980s were <a href="/wiki/Rachid_Mimouni" title="Rachid Mimouni">Rachid Mimouni</a>, later vice-president of <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tahar_Djaout" title="Tahar Djaout">Tahar Djaout</a>, murdered by an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamist" title="Islamist">Islamist</a> group in 1993 for his secularist views.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[224]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Malek_Bennabi" title="Malek Bennabi">Malek Bennabi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frantz_Fanon" title="Frantz Fanon">Frantz Fanon</a> are noted for their thoughts on <a href="/wiki/Decolonization" title="Decolonization">decolonization</a>; <a href="/wiki/Augustine_of_Hippo" title="Augustine of Hippo">Augustine of Hippo</a> was born in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tagaste" title="Tagaste">Tagaste</a> (modern-day <a href="/wiki/Souk_Ahras" title="Souk Ahras">Souk Ahras</a>); and <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Khaldun" title="Ibn Khaldun">Ibn Khaldun</a>, though born in <a href="/wiki/Tunis" title="Tunis">Tunis</a>, wrote the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muqaddima" title="Muqaddima">Muqaddima</a> while staying in Algeria. The works of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Senussi" title="Senussi">Sanusi</a> family in pre-colonial times, and of <a href="/wiki/Emir_Abdelkader" title="Emir Abdelkader">Emir Abdelkader</a> and Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Abdelhamid_Ben_Badis" title="Abdelhamid Ben Badis">Ben Badis</a> in colonial times, are widely noted. The Latin author <a href="/wiki/Apuleius" title="Apuleius">Apuleius</a> was born in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madaurus" title="Madaurus">Madaurus</a> (Mdaourouch), in what later became Algeria.
</p><p>Contemporary <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algerian_cinema" title="Algerian cinema">Algerian cinema</a> is various in terms of genre, exploring a wider range of themes and issues. There has been a transition from cinema which focused on the war of independence to films more concerned with the everyday lives of Algerians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[225]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Media_of_Algeria" title="Media of Algeria">Media of Algeria</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Portrait-racim.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="231" data-file-width="161" decoding="async" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Portrait-racim.jpg/140px-Portrait-racim.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3a/Portrait-racim.jpg 1.5x" width="140"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Portrait-racim.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Racim" title="Mohammed Racim">Mohammed Racim</a>; founder of the Algerian school for painting</div></div></div>
<p>Algerian painters, like <a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohamed_Racim" title="fr:Mohamed Racim">Mohamed Racim</a> or Baya, attempted to revive the prestigious Algerian past prior to French colonisation, at the same time that they have contributed to the preservation of the authentic values of Algeria. In this line, <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Temam" title="Mohamed Temam">Mohamed Temam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abdelkhader_Houamel" title="Abdelkhader Houamel">Abdelkhader Houamel</a> have also returned through this art, scenes from the history of the country, the habits and customs of the past and the country life. Other new artistic currents including the one of <a href="/wiki/M%27hamed_Issiakhem" title="M'hamed Issiakhem">M'hamed Issiakhem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Khadda" title="Mohammed Khadda">Mohammed Khadda</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bachir_Yelles" title="Bachir Yelles">Bachir Yelles</a>, appeared on the scene of Algerian painting, abandoning figurative classical painting to find new pictorial ways, in order to adapt Algerian paintings to the new realities of the country through its struggle and its aspirations. <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Khadda" title="Mohammed Khadda">Mohammed Khadda</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-art_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-art-231">[226]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/M%27hamed_Issiakhem" title="M'hamed Issiakhem">M'hamed Issiakhem</a> have been notable in recent years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-art_231-1"><a href="#cite_note-art-231">[226]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Algerian_literature" title="Algerian literature">Algerian literature</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Algerian_writers" title="List of Algerian writers">List of Algerian writers</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:242px;max-width:242px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:116px;max-width:116px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:147px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lucius_Apuleius_Platonicus,_from_%27Crabbes_Historical_Dictionary%27,_published_in_1825_(C19).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="719" data-file-width="558" decoding="async" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Lucius_Apuleius_Platonicus%2C_from_%27Crabbes_Historical_Dictionary%27%2C_published_in_1825_%28C19%29.jpg/228px-Lucius_Apuleius_Platonicus%2C_from_%27Crabbes_Historical_Dictionary%27%2C_published_in_1825_%28C19%29.jpg 2x" width="114"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Apuleius" title="Apuleius">Apuleius</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:122px;max-width:122px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:147px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kateb_Yacine_Nedjma_authograph.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2008" data-file-width="1627" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Kateb_Yacine_Nedjma_authograph.jpg/120px-Kateb_Yacine_Nedjma_authograph.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Kateb_Yacine_Nedjma_authograph.jpg/180px-Kateb_Yacine_Nedjma_authograph.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Kateb_Yacine_Nedjma_authograph.jpg/240px-Kateb_Yacine_Nedjma_authograph.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Kateb_Yacine" title="Kateb Yacine">Kateb Yacine</a></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>The historic roots of Algerian literature go back to the <a href="/wiki/Numidia" title="Numidia">Numidian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Africa_(Roman_province)" title="Africa (Roman province)">Roman African</a> era, when <a href="/wiki/Apuleius" title="Apuleius">Apuleius</a> wrote <i><a href="/wiki/The_Golden_Ass" title="The Golden Ass">The Golden Ass</a></i>, the only Latin novel to survive in its entirety. This period had also known <a href="/wiki/Augustine_of_Hippo" title="Augustine of Hippo">Augustine of Hippo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nonius_Marcellus" title="Nonius Marcellus">Nonius Marcellus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martianus_Capella" title="Martianus Capella">Martianus Capella</a>, among many others. The Middle Ages have known many Arabic writers who revolutionised the Arab world literature, with authors like <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_al-Buni" title="Ahmad al-Buni">Ahmad al-Buni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Manzur" title="Ibn Manzur">Ibn Manzur</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ibn_Khaldoun" title="Ibn Khaldoun">Ibn Khaldoun</a>, who wrote the <a href="/wiki/Muqaddimah" title="Muqaddimah">Muqaddimah</a> while staying in Algeria, and many others.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Albert_Camus" title="Albert Camus">Albert Camus</a> was an Algerian-born French Pied-Noir author. In 1957, he was awarded the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_literature" title="Nobel Prize in literature">Nobel Prize in literature</a>.
</p><p>Today Algeria contains, in its literary landscape, big names having not only marked the Algerian literature, but also the universal literary heritage in Arabic and French.
</p><p>As a first step, Algerian literature was marked by works whose main concern was the assertion of the Algerian national entity, there is the publication of novels as the <i>Algerian trilogy</i> of <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Dib" title="Mohammed Dib">Mohammed Dib</a>, or even <i>Nedjma</i> of <a href="/wiki/Kateb_Yacine" title="Kateb Yacine">Kateb Yacine</a> novel which is often regarded as a monumental and major work. Other known writers will contribute to the emergence of Algerian literature whom include <a href="/wiki/Mouloud_Feraoun" title="Mouloud Feraoun">Mouloud Feraoun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malek_Bennabi" title="Malek Bennabi">Malek Bennabi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malek_Haddad" title="Malek Haddad">Malek Haddad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moufdi_Zakaria" title="Moufdi Zakaria">Moufdi Zakaria</a>, Abdelhamid Ben Badis, Mohamed Laïd Al-Khalifa, <a href="/wiki/Mouloud_Mammeri" title="Mouloud Mammeri">Mouloud Mammeri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frantz_Fanon" title="Frantz Fanon">Frantz Fanon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Assia_Djebar" title="Assia Djebar">Assia Djebar</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ahlem_Mosteghanemi_at_Beirut_Book_Fair_2012.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1981" data-file-width="1688" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Ahlem_Mosteghanemi_at_Beirut_Book_Fair_2012.JPG/170px-Ahlem_Mosteghanemi_at_Beirut_Book_Fair_2012.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Ahlem_Mosteghanemi_at_Beirut_Book_Fair_2012.JPG/255px-Ahlem_Mosteghanemi_at_Beirut_Book_Fair_2012.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Ahlem_Mosteghanemi_at_Beirut_Book_Fair_2012.JPG/340px-Ahlem_Mosteghanemi_at_Beirut_Book_Fair_2012.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ahlem_Mosteghanemi_at_Beirut_Book_Fair_2012.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ahlam_Mosteghanemi" title="Ahlam Mosteghanemi">Ahlam Mosteghanemi</a>, the most widely read female writer in the <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[227]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In the aftermath of the independence, several new authors emerged on the Algerian literary scene, they will attempt through their works to expose a number of social problems, among them there are <a href="/wiki/Rachid_Boudjedra" title="Rachid Boudjedra">Rachid Boudjedra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rachid_Mimouni" title="Rachid Mimouni">Rachid Mimouni</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leila_Sebbar" title="Leila Sebbar">Leila Sebbar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tahar_Djaout" title="Tahar Djaout">Tahar Djaout</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tahir_Wattar" title="Tahir Wattar">Tahir Wattar</a>.
</p><p>Currently, a part of Algerian writers tends to be defined in a literature of shocking expression, due to the terrorism that occurred during the 1990s, the other party is defined in a different style of literature who staged an individualistic conception of the human adventure. Among the most noted recent works, there is the writer, <i>the swallows of Kabul</i> and <i>the attack</i> of <a href="/wiki/Yasmina_Khadra" title="Yasmina Khadra">Yasmina Khadra</a>, <i>the oath of barbarians</i> of <a href="/wiki/Boualem_Sansal" title="Boualem Sansal">Boualem Sansal</a>, <i>memory of the flesh</i> of <a href="/wiki/Ahlam_Mosteghanemi" title="Ahlam Mosteghanemi">Ahlam Mosteghanemi</a> and the last novel by Assia Djebar <i>nowhere in my father's House</i>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Algeria" title="Music of Algeria">Music of Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Anka.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1729" data-file-width="1326" decoding="async" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Anka.jpg/140px-Anka.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Anka.jpg/210px-Anka.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Anka.jpg/280px-Anka.jpg 2x" width="140"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Anka.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/El_Hadj_M%27Hamed_El_Anka" title="El Hadj M'Hamed El Anka">El Hadj M'Hamed El Anka</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Chaabi_(Algeria)" title="Chaabi (Algeria)">Chaâbi music</a> is a typically Algerian musical genre characterized by specific rhythms and of Qacidate (popular poems) in Arabic dialect. <a href="/wiki/El_Hadj_M%27Hamed_El_Anka" title="El Hadj M'Hamed El Anka">El Hadj M'Hamed El Anka</a> is considered the greatest master of the art in modern times. He wrote over 350 songs and produced some 130 records before his death in 1978. Many of his pupils went on to be renowned musicians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[228]</a></sup> The Constantinois <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andalusian_classical_music" title="Andalusian classical music">Malouf</a> style is saved by musician from whom <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Tahar_Fergani" title="Mohamed Tahar Fergani">Mohamed Tahar Fergani</a> is a performer.
</p><p>Folk music styles include <a href="/wiki/Bedouin_music" title="Bedouin music">Bedouin music</a>, characterized by the poetic songs based on long kacida (poems); Kabyle music, based on a rich repertoire that is poetry and old tales passed through generations; Shawiya music, a folklore from diverse areas of the <a href="/wiki/Aur%C3%A8s_Mountains" title="Aurès Mountains">Aurès Mountains</a>. Rahaba music style is unique to the Aures. <a href="/wiki/Souad_Massi" title="Souad Massi">Souad Massi</a> is a rising Algerian folk singer. Other Algerian singers of the diaspora include <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Manel_Filali&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Manel Filali (page does not exist)">Manel Filali</a> in <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kenza_Farah" title="Kenza Farah">Kenza Farah</a> in France. Tergui music is sung in <a href="/wiki/Tuareg_languages" title="Tuareg languages">Tuareg languages</a> generally, <a href="/wiki/Tinariwen" title="Tinariwen">Tinariwen</a> had a worldwide success. Finally, the staïfi music is born in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9tif" title="Sétif">Sétif</a> and remains a unique style of its kind.
</p><p>Modern music is available in several facets, <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%AF" title="Raï">Raï</a> music is a style typical of western Algeria. <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">Rap</a>, a relatively recent style in Algeria, is experiencing significant growth.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Algeria" title="Cinema of Algeria">Cinema of Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mohamed_LAKHDAR_HAMINA.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="482" data-file-width="911" decoding="async" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Mohamed_LAKHDAR_HAMINA.png/220px-Mohamed_LAKHDAR_HAMINA.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Mohamed_LAKHDAR_HAMINA.png/330px-Mohamed_LAKHDAR_HAMINA.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Mohamed_LAKHDAR_HAMINA.png/440px-Mohamed_LAKHDAR_HAMINA.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mohamed_LAKHDAR_HAMINA.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Lakhdar-Hamina" title="Mohammed Lakhdar-Hamina">Mohammed Lakhdar-Hamina</a>, one of the most prominent figures in contemporary Arabic cinema.</div></div></div>
<p>The Algerian state's interest in film-industry activities can be seen in the annual budget of DZD 200 million (EUR 1.3 million) allocated to production, specific measures and an ambitious programme plan implemented by the Ministry of Culture in order to promote national production, renovate the cinema stock and remedy the weak links in distribution and exploitation.
</p><p>The financial support provided by the state, through the Fund for the Development of the Arts, Techniques and the Film Industry (FDATIC) and the Algerian Agency for Cultural Influence (AARC), plays a key role in the promotion of national production. Between 2007 and 2013, FDATIC subsidised 98 films (feature films, documentaries and short films). In mid-2013, AARC had already supported a total of 78 films, including 42 feature films, 6 short films and 30 documentaries.
</p><p>According to the European Audiovisual Observatory's LUMIERE database, 41 Algerian films were distributed in Europe between 1996 and 2013; 21 films in this repertoire were Algerian-French co-productions. <a href="/wiki/Days_of_Glory_(2006_film)" title="Days of Glory (2006 film)"><i>Days of Glory</i> (2006)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Outside_the_Law_(2010_film)" title="Outside the Law (2010 film)"><i>Outside the Law</i> (2010)</a> recorded the highest number of admissions in the European Union, 3,172,612 and 474,722, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[229]</a></sup>
</p><p>Algeria won the <a href="/wiki/Palme_d%27Or" title="Palme d'Or">Palme d'Or</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/Chronicle_of_the_Years_of_Fire" title="Chronicle of the Years of Fire">Chronicle of the Years of Fire</a></i> (1975), two Oscars for <a href="/wiki/Z_(1969_film)" title="Z (1969 film)"><i>Z</i> (1969)</a>, and other awards for the Italian-Algerian movie <i><a href="/wiki/The_Battle_of_Algiers" title="The Battle of Algiers">The Battle of Algiers</a></i>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Algerian_cuisine" title="Algerian cuisine">Algerian cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Couscous_(Alg%C3%A9rie,_lieu_exact_non_pr%C3%A9cis%C3%A9).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Couscous_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%2C_lieu_exact_non_pr%C3%A9cis%C3%A9%29.jpg/170px-Couscous_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%2C_lieu_exact_non_pr%C3%A9cis%C3%A9%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Couscous_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%2C_lieu_exact_non_pr%C3%A9cis%C3%A9%29.jpg/255px-Couscous_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%2C_lieu_exact_non_pr%C3%A9cis%C3%A9%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Couscous_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%2C_lieu_exact_non_pr%C3%A9cis%C3%A9%29.jpg/340px-Couscous_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%2C_lieu_exact_non_pr%C3%A9cis%C3%A9%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Couscous_(Alg%C3%A9rie,_lieu_exact_non_pr%C3%A9cis%C3%A9).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Couscous" title="Couscous">Couscous</a>, the national dish of Algeria</div></div></div>
<p>Algerian cuisine is rich and diverse. The country was considered as the "granary of Rome". It offers a component of dishes and varied dishes, depending on the region and according to the seasons. The cuisine uses cereals as the main products, since they are always produced with abundance in the country. There is not a dish where cereals are not present.
</p><p>Algerian cuisine varies from one region to another, according to seasonal vegetables. It can be prepared using meat, fish and vegetables. Among the dishes known, <a href="/wiki/Couscous" title="Couscous">couscous</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WDL_235-0"><a href="#cite_note-WDL-235">[230]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chorba" title="Chorba">chorba</a>, rechta, chakhchoukha, berkoukes, <a href="/wiki/Shakshouka" title="Shakshouka">shakshouka</a>, mthewem, chtitha, mderbel, dolma, brik or bourek, garantita, lham'hlou, etc. <a href="/wiki/Merguez" title="Merguez">Merguez</a> sausage is widely used in Algeria, but it differs, depending on the region and on the added spices.
</p><p>Cakes are marketed and can be found in cities either in Algeria, in Europe or North America. However, traditional cakes are also made at home, following the habits and customs of each family. Among these cakes, there are Tamina, Baklawa, Chrik, Garn logzelles, Griouech, Kalb el-louz, Makroud, Mbardja, Mchewek, Samsa, Tcharak, Baghrir, Khfaf, Zlabia, Aarayech, Ghroubiya and Mghergchette. Algerian pastry also contains Tunisian or French cakes. Marketed and home-made bread products include varieties such as Kessra or Khmira or Harchaya, chopsticks and so-called washers Khoubz dar or Matloue. Other traditional meals sold often as street food include mhadjeb or mahjouba, karantika, doubara, chakhchoukha, hassouna, and t'chicha.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Algeria" title="Sport in Algeria">Sport in Algeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alg%C3%A9rie_-_Arm%C3%A9nie_-_20140531_-_Equipe_d%27Alg%C3%A9rie.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4928" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Alg%C3%A9rie_-_Arm%C3%A9nie_-_20140531_-_Equipe_d%27Alg%C3%A9rie.jpg/220px-Alg%C3%A9rie_-_Arm%C3%A9nie_-_20140531_-_Equipe_d%27Alg%C3%A9rie.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Alg%C3%A9rie_-_Arm%C3%A9nie_-_20140531_-_Equipe_d%27Alg%C3%A9rie.jpg/330px-Alg%C3%A9rie_-_Arm%C3%A9nie_-_20140531_-_Equipe_d%27Alg%C3%A9rie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Alg%C3%A9rie_-_Arm%C3%A9nie_-_20140531_-_Equipe_d%27Alg%C3%A9rie.jpg/440px-Alg%C3%A9rie_-_Arm%C3%A9nie_-_20140531_-_Equipe_d%27Alg%C3%A9rie.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alg%C3%A9rie_-_Arm%C3%A9nie_-_20140531_-_Equipe_d%27Alg%C3%A9rie.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Algeria_national_football_team" title="Algeria national football team">Algeria national football team</a></div></div></div>
<p>Various games have existed in Algeria since antiquity. In the <a href="/wiki/Aur%C3%A8s_Mountains" title="Aurès Mountains">Aures</a>, people played several games such as El Kherba or El khergueba (<a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">chess</a> variant). Playing cards, <a href="/wiki/Checkers" title="Checkers">checkers</a> and chess games are part of Algerian culture. Racing (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fantasia_(culture)" title="Fantasia (culture)">fantasia</a>) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rifle_shooting" title="Rifle shooting">rifle shooting</a> are part of cultural recreation of the Algerians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[231]</a></sup>
</p><p>The first Algerian and African gold medalist is <a href="/wiki/Boughera_El_Ouafi" title="Boughera El Ouafi">Boughera El Ouafi</a> in <a href="/wiki/1928_Summer_Olympics" title="1928 Summer Olympics">1928 Olympics of Amsterdam</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Marathon" title="Marathon">Marathon</a>. The second Algerian Medalist was <a href="/wiki/Alain_Mimoun" title="Alain Mimoun">Alain Mimoun</a> in <a href="/wiki/1956_Summer_Olympics" title="1956 Summer Olympics">1956 Summer Olympics</a> in Melbourne. Several men and women were champions in athletics in the 1990s including <a href="/wiki/Noureddine_Morceli" title="Noureddine Morceli">Noureddine Morceli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hassiba_Boulmerka" title="Hassiba Boulmerka">Hassiba Boulmerka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nouria_M%C3%A9rah-Benida" title="Nouria Mérah-Benida">Nouria Merah-Benida</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Taoufik_Makhloufi" title="Taoufik Makhloufi">Taoufik Makhloufi</a>, all specialized in <a href="/wiki/Middle-distance_running" title="Middle-distance running">middle-distance running</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[232]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Football_in_Algeria" title="Football in Algeria">Football</a> is the most popular sport in Algeria. Several names are engraved in the history of the sport, including <a href="/wiki/Lakhdar_Belloumi" title="Lakhdar Belloumi">Lakhdar Belloumi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rachid_Mekhloufi" title="Rachid Mekhloufi">Rachid Mekhloufi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hac%C3%A8ne_Lalmas" title="Hacène Lalmas">Hassen Lalmas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rabah_Madjer" title="Rabah Madjer">Rabah Madjer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Riyad_Mahrez" title="Riyad Mahrez">Riyad Mahrez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salah_Assad" title="Salah Assad">Salah Assad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Djamel_Zidane" title="Djamel Zidane">Djamel Zidane</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Algeria_national_football_team" title="Algeria national football team">Algeria national football team</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">1982 FIFA World Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1986 FIFA World Cup">1986 FIFA World Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 FIFA World Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a>. In addition, several football clubs have won continental and international trophies as the club <a href="/wiki/ES_S%C3%A9tif" title="ES Sétif">ES Sétif</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JS_Kabylia" title="JS Kabylia">JS Kabylia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Football_Federation" title="Algerian Football Federation">Algerian Football Federation</a> is an association of Algeria football clubs organizing national competitions and international matches of the selection of Algeria national football team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[233]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Explanatory_notes">Explanatory notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Explanatory notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">

</li>
<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <i><a href="/wiki/The_World_Factbook" title="The World Factbook">CIA World Factbook</a></i> states that about 15% of Algerians, a minority, identify as Berber even though many Algerians have Berber origins. The Factbook explains that of the approximately 15% who identify as Berber, most live in the <a href="/wiki/Kabylia" title="Kabylia">Kabylia</a> region, more closely identify with Berber heritage instead of Arab heritage, and are Muslim.</span>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Citations">Citations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Citations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
